## Thread: DBCS G datatype -> X datatype — 2 msgs

### DBCS G datatype -> X datatype

- **From:** "Nikolay I. Nikolskiy" <nik@tepkom.ru>
- **Date:** 2001-11-01T15:22:06+03:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9rrepc$1a14$1@news.spbu.ru>`

```
Is it possible to move value of DBCS variable or G literal into MIXED (X)
variable?

Thank you, nikolay.
-------------------------------------
http://nik.tepkom.ru
```

#### ↳ Re: DBCS G datatype -> X datatype

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-01T15:04:14-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9rsdb7$93r$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<9rrepc$1a14$1@news.spbu.ru>`

```
You don't mention which compiler (or operating system) you are using.  Most
of the "old" compilers that used to support PIC G rather than PIC N are now
"out-of-date" if not out of service.  However, for the general question and
GUESSING that you might be using an OLD IBM compiler, look at the following:

 http://publib.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/BOOKS/igypg205/1.6.6?

Look particularly at IGZCA2D and IGZCD2A
```

## Thread: E-mail from COBOL program — 1 this month / 5 total

_Thread started [2001-10](2001-10.md#t-49730bab44)._

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: E-mail from COBOL program

- **From:** rtwolfe@flexus.com (Bob Wolfe)
- **Date:** 2001-11-01T13:31:35+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3be14d3c.1147277@news.epix.net>`
- **References:** `<3bdcb6bd_1@news1.prserv.net> <9rlkf1$8dt$1@usenet.otenet.gr> <3be0de1d_4@news1.prserv.net>`

```
"Stephen Plotnick" <thepla@attglobal.net> wrote:

>I use Realia Workbench 3.1. I do not think they have "COM" server. I will
>call support and let you know. Thanks.

Stephen:

COBOL sp2 supports Realia Workbench 3.1 and supports embedded OCX
(Active X) controls (com objects).  You can send and receive e-mail
through one of these.  Although I don't know of anyone using one of
these with Groupwise, I don't see why it wouldn't work.

I also believe that Thane Hubbell has developed a solution for
sending/receiving e-mail messages with an add-on tool to sp2.

In addition, Neil Williamson has developed an add-on tool for sp2
which allows intergration of Microsoft Office applications in your sp2
application.  This will allow you to send/receive e-mail through
Outlook Express.

These tools also work with our Thin Client software, so you could even
run your e-mail application on a server in one location and allow
clients in remote locations to run the application and send e-mail.

If we can be of assistance, please send a private e-mail message to
rtwolfe@flexus.com.



>"Panos Zotos" <pzotos@syntax.gr> wrote in message
>news:9rlkf1$8dt$1@usenet.otenet.gr...
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
>


Bob Wolfe
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
When replying by e-mail, make sure that you correct the e-mail address.
Check out The Flexus COBOL Page at http://www.flexus.com
```

<a id="t-beb9b9e7da"></a>
## Thread: How do you count? — 15 this month / 73 total

_Thread started [2001-10](2001-10.md#t-beb9b9e7da)._

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Subscript wish

_(thread depth: 13)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-01T20:31:02+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BE1B106.C037F643@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<Pq4C7.12962$W91.84957@news1.wwck1.ri.home.com> <o6gitt4o1k73s101rn9ovdm53ms772o9j0@4ax.com> <56dC7.10232$ym4.448959@iad-read.news.verio.net> <sYfC7.67$VF.215295@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net> <FmgC7.10250$ym4.449477@iad-read.news.verio.net> <9rjt19$2vm$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <9rkc5h$iuj$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net> <9rkdgj$f1q$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <9rkht2$bq$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <9rkiuh$2aus$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <YzyD7.11178$U7.566797@bin1.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
Howard Brazee wrote:
> 
> If the
> warehouse has bins labeled 5000-5999, our code should match.   (In my case
> it is the account book, but you know what I mean)

I am in complete _dis_agreement with you.  If one particular warehouse
has bins number 5000-5999 (or accounts) then the _DATA_FILE_ should
match this and the code should process the data accordingly regardless
of what the _actual_ codes are.

What are you suggesting - a unique version of the program for each
warehouse (or department, company, division) and a rewrite of the system
if a new row of racking is added ?  If they move to a new warehouse will
you throw out all the programs and start again ?

In the Accounts file have a flag that indicates 'special processing'. 
Read the accounts file and pick up all those so marked.  These _may_
co-incidentally be all in the range 5000-5999 at one point in time.

> but wherever possible the code should look like the business environment. 

But building codes into the program is only following the _current_
business environment, it is then becoming a _constraint_ on it.

While originally those special codes were set to 5000-5999 in some
arbitrary way, they now _must_ be in that range because of the program. 
It is no longer the program looking like the business, the business must
look like the program.

If an account is needed to be changed from being special to not or vice
versa, the original must have all its transactions reversed then be
deleted and a new code set up with all the transactions added back just
to put it in range or out of it.

With a _properly_designed_ system the account (or bin) should be able to
be added or removed from the special range with a flag or other
indication.

For example if these were Customer accounts and the program treated
customers in the range 5000-5999 as being on 'stop supply' because they
hadn't paid for 3 months or were over their credit limit, then they
would have to be deleted and recreated to put them in this range or out
of it as appropriate, and all their transactions and history would also
be deleted and recreated.

If this mechanism actually was implemented then the programmer may well
claim that the program followed the business practice.  No - it enforced
the business practice.
```

```

On  1-Nov-2001, Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote:

> If this mechanism actually was implemented then the programmer may well
> claim that the program followed the business practice.  No - it enforced
> the business practice.

You can say that about virtually any business rule codified in a program.

Leave the business rules out, take out the input and output, and you will
never need to do maintenance!
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Subscript wish

_(thread depth: 15)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T07:04:37+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BE24585.32AAFC97@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<Pq4C7.12962$W91.84957@news1.wwck1.ri.home.com> <o6gitt4o1k73s101rn9ovdm53ms772o9j0@4ax.com> <56dC7.10232$ym4.448959@iad-read.news.verio.net> <sYfC7.67$VF.215295@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net> <FmgC7.10250$ym4.449477@iad-read.news.verio.net> <9rjt19$2vm$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <9rkc5h$iuj$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net> <9rkdgj$f1q$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <9rkht2$bq$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <9rkiuh$2aus$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <YzyD7.11178$U7.566797@bin1.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <3BE1B106.C037F643@Azonic.co.nz> <9rrp69$55f$1@peabody.colorado.edu>`

```
Howard Brazee wrote:
> 
> On  1-Nov-2001, Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote:
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> You can say that about virtually any business rule codified in a program.

The issue is the extent to which the program constrains the business.  

There was an example a couple of months ago where the program
implemented special processing of customer and product combinations with
a huge nested IF .. ELSE with the actual customer and sales codes buried
in the same code repeated in several programs.  Obviously a 'quick fix'
that had grown out of hand.  There is now no possible way of testing
whether those codes are correct and that the program works as required
without an enormous and exhaustive amount of test data.

If the accounts and sales codes had been flagged to indicate their
status, or a file of combinations had been built to indicate which were
appropriate then:

  a) the actual business rules could be proven with subset test data.
  b) the actual data combinations could be inspected and changed by
those responsible.
  c) 'maintenance' would involve changing the data, not rewriting the
programs.

In your case you are not only implementing the business rules into the
program, you are also implementing the data items to which these rules
apply.  Your bin number example is more clear, but is just the same as
the accounts.  Why would you write a program that specifies exactly what
the bin numbers in a warehouse should be ?

I probably go too far the other way and have a data file of 'decodes',
lots of very simple data items that the user can maintain that also
includes optional flags.  The program implements different sets of
business rules the data files (maintained by the user) specifies where
these rules apply.  This reduces the program maintenance for trivial
changes and allows the user (rather than the programmer) to control how
the system works.  It also means that the user must understand how the
_business_ operates rather than just accepting what the programmer
coded.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Subscript wish

_(thread depth: 16)_

- **From:** "James J. Gavan" <jjgavan@home.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-01T18:49:12+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BE19920.D68AF7E6@home.com>`
- **References:** `<Pq4C7.12962$W91.84957@news1.wwck1.ri.home.com> <o6gitt4o1k73s101rn9ovdm53ms772o9j0@4ax.com> <56dC7.10232$ym4.448959@iad-read.news.verio.net> <sYfC7.67$VF.215295@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net> <FmgC7.10250$ym4.449477@iad-read.news.verio.net> <9rjt19$2vm$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <9rkc5h$iuj$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net> <9rkdgj$f1q$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <9rkht2$bq$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <9rkiuh$2aus$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <YzyD7.11178$U7.566797@bin1.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <3BE1B106.C037F643@Azonic.co.nz> <9rrp69$55f$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <3BE24585.32AAFC97@Azonic.co.nz>`

```


Richard Plinston wrote:

> Howard Brazee wrote:
> >
…[42 more quoted lines elided]…
> coded.

Perhaps the best one I can think of to support what Richard is stressing - 30
years ago at Debenhams department store group. The former accountant of Harvey
Nichols, (the other 'snotty' store just down the road from Harrods of
Knightsbridge),  as a result of centralization, was based in West country with
us computer geeks. We were coming up to VAT and it seemed logical to re-design
the Chart-of-Accounts. He's a bean counter, so he knows all about account coding
systems - Right ?

So he pored through the coding systems being used by some 60 stores to come up
with a generic list. In the case of Payroll we produced pre-printed Journal
sheets to make it easier for the store accountants.

Having been 'caught' before, I designed the computer system, (Chart of
Accounts), to have 'flags' indicating which group each account belonged to, i.e.
Flag 1 = Current Assets, Flag-2 = Fixed Assets, etc. (Plus there were 'fillers'
so the flag system was expandable). I kept telling the 'committee' I was doing
this but it went over the heads of the bean counters as computerese.

There we are about a month away from VAT and he issues his list of account
codes  - all hell broke loose. Back came the store accountants, 'this' was
missing, and 'that' was missing. The committee looked on glumly when he admitted
to the shortcomings and said some of the additions required would break his
numeric groupings !

Then the bean counters got the message. I reiterated "I don't give a damn about
his groupings. I have made the computer system use flags, regardless of his
coding system". Phew ! Sighs of relief all around - but he 'hated' me for having
provided the solution.

AND - back 40 years ago when we were first cutting our teeth - the Marketing
Manager *insisted* our Customer Account numbers MUST include the salesman's
number, (to find out who is selling what).. We insisted, just as strongly, that
they wouldn't be included - we keypunched the individual Salesmen's numbers from
Order forms.. Six months later he revamped his sales territories !

Jimmy
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: How do you count?

_(thread depth: 8)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-01T20:06:08+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BE1AB30.724557E2@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<Pq4C7.12962$W91.84957@news1.wwck1.ri.home.com> <o6gitt4o1k73s101rn9ovdm53ms772o9j0@4ax.com> <56dC7.10232$ym4.448959@iad-read.news.verio.net> <sYfC7.67$VF.215295@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net> <FmgC7.10250$ym4.449477@iad-read.news.verio.net> <PYzD7.5933$xS6.6664@www.newsranger.com>`

```
Charles wrote:
> 
> A person should not have to start counting at zero, the compiler
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> what makes common sense every time you want to use an array.

It _isn't_ 'counting', it is numerating, a completely different thing.

Counting is where you determine how many things there are.  In an array
one may count how many of the array items have data in them, if the only
items with data are those numbered 2, 7 and 9 then counting these gives
3.

Numerating is giving numbers to things.  In the case of array items
numerating gives a number to each item by which it may be referenced. 
Usually these are sequential and contiguous, though they need not be,
all that is required is a predictable and repeatable numeration.

'What makes common sense' is entrirely what one is used to.  You can't
cope with numerations other than those used in Cobol.  This doesn't make
Cobol's better or 'common sense', it just makes you less able to cope
with other mechanisms.
 
> This is just lousy compiler implementation.

It has nothing to do with 'compiler implementation', it is a language
design issue.


> Why make an object oriented compiler that lets you make up your own
> english names for all of your code and then subtract 1 from what makes
> sense to normal people.  

So now you assert that Cobol programmers are 'normal' and others are
not.

As Object Orientated _Languages_ allow one to write one's own way of
programming then it is inherent in any OOL that whatever numeration
required can be implemented and used. If you feel that something is
'normal' for you then feel free to do this in the OOL, because it will
allow it.


> I don't want to have to subtract one from
> everything because someone failed to make a good compiler.  

It is nothing to do with the compiler, it is a language design issue.

And given that the OOL will allow you to use it is any way that you care
to implement, then it will only be your failure (and not the language's
or the compiler's) if it doesn't work the way that you require.

> It just doesnt
> make sense to force people to do something so unnatural.  

All numerations are 'unnatural', they are all completely artificial
being the invention of man.

> Programs should
> be made to serve people; People should not have to be slaves to a computer.

Yet you seem to be a slave to a numeration starting at 1 and
incrementing by 1.

I say: let people be free to create whatever numerations they wish. 
There is absolutely no reason why the numerations of an array should be
contiguous, evenly incrementing, or indeed in sequence.

If I want an array with items: 42, 7, 19, 55, 72, -3 - a total of 6
occurances, then why not.

       01  My-Table.
           03  My-Table-Item                OCCURS 6 
                                            INDEXES 42, 7, 19, 55, 72,
-3
                                            INDEXED BY My-Index
            05 My-Table-Flag                PIC X.

          MOVE "Y"             TO My-Table-Flag(55).

          PERFORM
              VARYING My-Index OVER INDEXES
    
              IF ( My-Table-Flag(My-Index) = "Y" )
                  ...
          END-PERFORM
```

On Thu, 01 Nov 2001 20:06:08 +0000, in article <3BE1AB30.724557E2@Azonic.co.nz>,
Richard Plinston stated 
>
>Charles wrote:

Starting to count at Zero and numerating are two different things.

What I was saying is this:  
The COBOL compiler has an index that starts at Zero, but it lets the 
programmer start counting at 1.  Then the compiler subtracts one
to made up the difference.  Using this system when the programmer wants the 
number 3 item in a list of occurs, then he just says move table-item (3) to a
given location or whatever.  This is simpler for a human being to figure out,
and makes perfect sense.  

I say the COBOL compiler's approach to this subject makes more common sense 
than C++ or JAVA.  That is my personal opinion.  I took classes in all three
languages and I know there are plenty of things each language does better than
the other.  Pascal also lets you select the starting and ending number in an
array and do a number of complicated techniques to construct complex data types
on the fly.

COBOL can't really enumerate.  You can build an index inside the table that can
be searched with the search verb, but that isnt exactly the same thing, and
takes up valuabel space.  You could also convert your bin number to the occurs
just like in C++ you would have to subtract 1 to find the right array element.

>> 
>> A person should not have to start counting at zero, the compiler
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Numerating is a valid concept, but it has nothing to do with starting to count
at zero.  Numerating is giving an alternate token or variable name to a
variable, and allowing the alternate variable name to be used in its place.

>Numerating is giving numbers to things.  In the case of array items
>numerating gives a number to each item by which it may be referenced. 
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>
The COBOL language was designed to let the programmer start counting at one, 
and the compiler was forced to implement that concept to meets the needs of
the COBOL standard.
>
>> Why make an object oriented compiler that lets you make up your own
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>
It doesn't make sense to count starting at zero???????

I don't go to the store and say here take zero cents and give the clerk 
a penny.  Do you do that?  Would that be normal to you?

Get real!


Just because some computer language forced you to count starting at zero,
doesnt make it normal.  Why should anyone be forced to do such an insane thing.
Computers should be user friendly.  The whole concept behind the development of
COBOL was that it was suppose to be a language that was written in a readable 
fashion.  

But now you are still waiting to make your first Zero million dollars.

Does this make sense to you?

I admit  that COBOL can not enumerate.  I suggest you turn your idea into the
standards committe and wait 20 years to see if it happens.  Either that or get a
compiler manufacturer to add it in as an extra add-on to their compiler, or get
an object oriented compiler.  If you could build a hash code for the index that
might be interesting.  Instead of an array you could make a set!

I could still be waiting to earn my Zero'th Dollar!!!!!

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: How do you count?

_(thread depth: 9)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T16:12:39+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BE2C5F7.1D4E8BE8@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<Pq4C7.12962$W91.84957@news1.wwck1.ri.home.com> <o6gitt4o1k73s101rn9ovdm53ms772o9j0@4ax.com> <56dC7.10232$ym4.448959@iad-read.news.verio.net> <sYfC7.67$VF.215295@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net> <FmgC7.10250$ym4.449477@iad-read.news.verio.net> <PYzD7.5933$xS6.6664@www.newsranger.com> <3BE1AB30.724557E2@Azonic.co.nz>`

```
Charles wrote:

> The COBOL compiler has an index that starts at Zero, 

No.  It has nothing that 'starts at zero'.  Items in Working Storage
start at whatever byte address after the previous item.

> but it lets the programmer start counting at 1.

It _isn't_ 'counting', it is numerating, a completely different thing.

> Then the compiler subtracts one to made up the difference. 

No, usually it multiplies by the item size and adds an offset to some
point in the data area to arrive at the correct byte address. I doubt
that you will actually find any compiler that 'subracts 1'. The actual
details are usually not particularly relevant anyway.

>  Using this system when the programmer wants the 
> number 3 item in a list of occurs, then he just says move table-item (3) to a
> given location or whatever.  This is simpler for a human being to figure out,
> and makes perfect sense.  

What makes 'perfect sense' is usually entirely what one is used to.

One thread here has a request to be able to access 'number 3' with
table-item(5002).  In general my array accesses are done with variables
as subscripts, I doubt that there is _any_ program that I have written
with 'table-item(3)', nor indeed many programmers that would use literal
subscripts to any great extent.  Your example is a straw-man.

> Numerating is a valid concept, but it has nothing to do with starting 
> to count at zero.  

Array indexing or subscripting has nothing to do with counting. 

> Numerating is giving an alternate token or variable name to a
> variable, and allowing the alternate variable name to be used in its place.
 
Numerating is giving numbers to things.  In the case of array items
numerating gives a number to each item by which it may be referenced. In
the case of Cobol all arrays are numerated as 1, 2, 3, 4, ... n.

I don't know where you got the idea of an _alternate_ token, but there
may be a case where this is _also_ a form of numerating.

Other examples of numerating are House numbers in a street, Post Office
box numbers, car licence plates, Bank accounts.  Some start at 1, some
at zero, some at other numbers, such as 1001.

> The COBOL language was designed to let the programmer start counting at one, 
> and the compiler was forced to implement that concept to meets the needs of
> the COBOL standard.

Array indexing or subscripting has nothing to do with counting. 

I don't see the compiler being 'forced' to implement anything, it does
so willingly.  I also don't see that your original:

>> This is just lousy compiler implementation.

has any meaning.  Was it 'forced' to be 'lousy' ?  Of course not, it
just implemented the language.

> It doesn't make sense to count starting at zero???????

Array indexing or subscripting has nothing to do with counting. 

> I don't go to the store and say here take zero cents and give the clerk 
> a penny.  Do you do that?  Would that be normal to you?
 
I also don't give 200 individual cents for a $2.00 item.  Giving money
to a clerk has nothing to do with array indexing, or numerating. 

> Just because some computer language forced you to count starting at zero,
> doesnt make it normal.

Array indexing or subscripting has nothing to do with counting. 

> I admit  that COBOL can not enumerate. 

I am not sure why you 'admit' this.  I suspect that you are taking a
very limited specific view of what 'enunmeration' is, such as defined
for 'enum' in the C language, and believing that to be the only
definition.

While Cobol does not do 'C enum' it does actually enumerate the arrays,
giving each array item a number.
```

## Thread: Implementing const in COBOL — 9 this month / 15 total

_Thread started [2001-10](2001-10.md#t-74d5339b8e)._

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Implementing const in COBOL

- **From:** chris.glazier@microfocus.com (Chris Glazier)
- **Date:** 2001-11-01T08:38:34-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<260cd566.0111010838.282b6412@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<bfbb8fd4.0110310527.92e1703@posting.google.com> <jd%D7.3495$3t1.748166323@newssvr30.news.prodigy.com>`

```
Standard COBOL does have this mechanism, it is: CALL ...USING BY
CONTENT ...

This causes a copy of the data item to be passed by reference and
therefore the original item will be protected. In Some COBOL
implementations (like Net Express) you can directly use a literal in
the USING and it will automatically be converted to BY CONTENT.

"Edwin Earl Ross" <EdwinEarl@yahoo.com> wrote in message news:<jd%D7.3495$3t1.748166323@newssvr30.news.prodigy.com>...
> There is neither a C-like const in Standard COBOL nor #DEFINE <name>
> <value>. Consequently, values in data items are not protected; they are
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
> > M Shetty
```

- **From:** "Robert Sales" <Robert.Sales@merant.com>

- **Message-ID:** `<9rtoor$a7j$1@hyperion.eu.merant.com>`
- **References:** `<bfbb8fd4.0110310527.92e1703@posting.google.com> <jd%D7.3495$3t1.748166323@newssvr30.news.prodigy.com> <260cd566.0111010838.282b6412@posting.google.com> <45rE7.152927$3d2.5426455@bgtnsc06-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
The ability to specify Working-storage elements in the PROCEDURE DIVISION
USING header is definitely a feature, and documented in the Language
Reference Manual.  I think this was originally added for compatibility with
some dialect or other, but is actually quite useful (and efficient) for
purely input parameters.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Implementing const in COBOL

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** KNeddy@home.com
- **Date:** 2001-11-03T07:30:21+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3be39281.141172569@NEWS>`
- **References:** `<bfbb8fd4.0110310527.92e1703@posting.google.com> <jd%D7.3495$3t1.748166323@newssvr30.news.prodigy.com> <260cd566.0111010838.282b6412@posting.google.com> <45rE7.152927$3d2.5426455@bgtnsc06-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```

>
>    In a subprogram I accidently put a group item referenced in the
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Do I understand this to mean that the subprogram had the working
storage group item...or the "main" (program that made the call) had
the group item?  I'm guessing that you mean the subprogram, which
would make sense to me. The sub program will change the data in the
working storage section, but once control is returned to the "main"
program...that group-level-item (the one in the working storage
section of the subprogram) would no longer exist. The group item in
the main program would remain unchanged since it was not passed
correctly to the sub program. You could do a simple 
"Move ws-group-level-item To linkage-section-group-level-item." 
That would allow the linkage section group level item to be "changed".
I'm not sure why you would ever want to do it that way.

If you indeed put the group item in the linkage section of the "main"
program, it would indeed reside in memory while the sub program is
executing. If you were using a debugger to view that group level item,
then you would see it that there is a value in it.  However,  the
working storage group-level-item  in the subprogram would be the
value(s) changed. Not the linkage group level items.  Why? Because you
didn't pass the group level item correctly.

If you call a program using a four byte field, then as long as you
have a field that four bytes can reside in, the compiler may not care
about it being a working storage field. If  however, you try to link
that program and you do not have a field to put the four bytes in, I
am guessing the compiler would flag it. That's my guess as to what
happened. I could be wrong.

I would think of it as a feature and not a bug.
```

<KNeddy@home.com> wrote in message news:3be40db5.90701311@NEWS...
> On Sat, 03 Nov 2001 21:28:37 +0000, Richard Plinston
> <riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote:
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
> encountered it before.

You might also want to take a look at the "INITIAL" verb for use in the
subroutine.  You can do the same thing there, so that the mainline does not
have to be aware of the fact that the subroutine does not retain it's values
from call to call.  Compiling the subroutine with the INITIAL statement has
the same effect as using the CANCEL after each call.

Donald.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Implementing const in COBOL

_(thread depth: 8)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-03T20:04:24-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9s27ll$7o8$1@slb3.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<bfbb8fd4.0110310527.92e1703@posting.google.com> <jd%D7.3495$3t1.748166323@newssvr30.news.prodigy.com> <260cd566.0111010838.282b6412@posting.google.com> <45rE7.152927$3d2.5426455@bgtnsc06-news.ops.worldnet.att.net> <3be39281.141172569@NEWS> <3BE46185.2AEE4A44@Azonic.co.nz> <3be40db5.90701311@NEWS> <5DUE7.35737$6h5.3330198@news20.bellglobal.com>`

```
Donald's note might be a little "confusing".

The INITIAL attribute in the PROGRAM-ID paragraph "guarantees" that each
time the subprogram is called, that its storage items are placed into
"initial state" (not kept from the last time).

The INITIALIZE verb (or statement) may be used in either a subprogram or a
main program to place a specific 01-level into "initial state".  This is NOT
what actually happens (as filler and unnamed items are NOT impacted by the
INITIALIZE statement) - but it is "similar" to what happens.
```

## Thread: ms sql preprocessor — 5 msgs

_Topics: [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases)_

### ms sql preprocessor

- **From:** csmith@escape.com (Charlie Smith)
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T16:39:27+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3be2ca39.357356321@news.escape.com>`

```
Hello All!

I've been given the task of working on the database bridge component
of my company's product and I'm looking at alternatives to the 'ugly'
mess of C++ code using ACE, RogueWave and whatever else to allow easy
development on both Windows and *NIX systems.

The target platform (for the moment) is Win 2000.  We are using
NetExpress 3.1 under a product called Unikix.  I must support both
Oracle and MS SQL databases.

I have managed to get a COBOL program to compile AND run successfully
against out Oracle database.  Just took a little digging to find the
COBOL SQL preprocessor.

The problem I've run into is the 'lack' of and COBOL preprocesor for
MS SQL.  Does any use this combination?  What are your
recommendations?  I've looked at the OpenESQL documentation and I just
don't know if it fits the bill.

BTW, does anyone know of any other transaction processing systems like
IBM's CICS?  The product we're using (Unikix) is a pretty good
likeness however Sun recently purchased it and plans to only support
the Sun platform.  Kind of kills our AIX and Windows installations.

Thanks in advance.

Charlie Smith
```

I'm currently in the process of testing using Net Express 3.1 and MS

coding as 'neutral' as possible - i.e., not dedicated to specific features
in one version of a DB.

appears in table classes. Your comment about the preprocessor - check the
on-line help book for ESQL/SQL - you have to load the ODBC driver supplied
with N/E.

#### ↳ Re: ms sql preprocessor

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-03T14:44:28+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3be34d4b_2@news.newsgroups.com>`
- **References:** `<3be2ca39.357356321@news.escape.com>`

```
Charlie,

You have received some good responses and Jimmy is sending you code so I'll
keep this short.

The connection between COBOL and SQL is achieved by the SQL pre-processor.
This is independent of ANY Relational Database so the same COBOL SHOULD be
able to connect to MS SQL (for SQL Server or ACCESS) AND Oracle, PROVIDED
the table structures are identical. (In fact, you should be able to run
against, INGRES, ACCESS, or DB2 or UDB on a mainframe, given the same table
structures and column names.)

This miracle is achieved by the use of a separate connection to the target
RDB which occurs at run time and is system dependent. It is called Open
Database Connectivity (ODBC) and your COBOL will talk to ANY database for
which there is an ODBC driver available on your system and which has the
ODBC connection activated. Under Windows you do this through the Control
Panel and ODBC32. The exercise of setting this up is separate to the
exercise of writing your COBOL code.

As long as you avoid RDB specific constructs (like Oracle Procedures) and
simply use the RDB as a receptacle, driven from COBOL, your DB access (SQL)
will be portable.

It works and I've done it in both mainframe (accessing mainframe databases
from the PC) and PC environments. It isn't even difficult.

Pete.


"Charlie Smith" <csmith@escape.com> wrote in message
news:3be2ca39.357356321@news.escape.com...

## Thread: Recent College Graduate needs advice — 3 msgs

### Recent College Graduate needs advice

- **From:** tammy9305@yahoo.com (tammy)
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T09:20:02-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<5feebebe.0111020920.40f0659f@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi, I am a recent computer science graduate of DePaul university. I
have been looking for an entry level full time position for the past
three months and I finally got a nible. The problem is I have never
had a phone interview and I really don't know what to expect. I really
need this job so I want to prepare myself as much as possible. The
position in and entry level programmer/analyst. Below is the job
description, can someone please tell me wher I can find some quick
reference for COBOL and C++. I took a class in both and did pretty
well but that was school and this is real life. Again, I really want
this position and I am a really quick study. Can someone please tell
me what kinds of questions I should prepare to answer. I know the is a
java forum but I was hoping one of you professional programmers can
point me in the right direction. Any help would be greatly
appreciated.


Role: Programmer Analyst (COOL Developer)

The Programmer Analyst is responsible for developing and managing the
application code and user interface (UI) components for a basic system
on the products and services team. (These systems can include the base
TBA
System, desktop applications, IVR systems, or Internet/intranet
applications.)
The Programmer Analyst works closely with other programmer analysts, 
quality assurance analysts, and systems analysts, with tasks in the
following
categories:

Planning and design. The Programmer Analyst takes the specifications 
from the Systems Analyst and then determines the detailed tasks
required to
create the code and UI.

Developing the application code and UI components. The Programmer 
Analyst builds the code and UI components according to the functional 
specifications and detailed design.

Other specific responsibilities in development include:
Working with the Systems Analyst to clarify and improve the design as
required. He or she may also prepare user documentation and will unit 
test each piece of code to verify the basic functionality before
passing it along
for more comprehensive testing. Throughout the project, the programmer
analyst
consistently uses code management tools to avoid versioning problems.

Role Requirements

Problem solving and decision making
Learning agility
Client responsiveness
Project execution
Project analysis and planning
Technical Skills
Structured programming, design, and language(s) such as COBOL or C
Operating systems
Relational databases and data models (ex. DB2, Oracle or Access)
Source code management
Editing, compiling, and debugging tools
Creating user and technical documentation

Years of Relevant Experience Required: 0-4 years
Travel Required: None

COOL stands for COBOL Object-Oriented Language. It utilizes some of
the
skills involved in both COBOL and C++ programming.

Again ANY HELP WOULD BE GREATLY APPRECIATED.
```

#### ↳ Re: Recent College Graduate needs advice

- **From:** Charles <nospam@newsranger.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T20:52:32+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<kIDE7.10557$xS6.14606@www.newsranger.com>`
- **References:** `<5feebebe.0111020920.40f0659f@posting.google.com>`

```
On 2 Nov 2001 09:20:02 -0800, in article
<5feebebe.0111020920.40f0659f@posting.google.com>, tammy stated 
>

If you have ever written any kind of interactive program in COBOL or CICS or C++
or Visual Basic, you should stress that.  Especially if you are good at object
oriented concepts like one might learn in JAVA.  Often an interview will ask you
how many programs you have written, or how long the programs were. If you worked
in the computer lab you should stress that a little.

They will probably want to know what kind of operating sytems you have
experience on and what kind of hardware.  Windows, OS/390, VM, VSE/ESA, IBM PC,
Compilers, Office Suites, LINUX, AS400, etc.  

They may also want to know about your experience with Server Data and Network
Systems/topologies.  Windows NT, Windows XP, Windows 2000, Apache, Novell
Netware, CISCO Routers, TCP/IP, HTML, CGI, Pearl, etc. 

The requirements for the job did say Zero to four years experience, so you
should stress your ultra High GPA "if that is the case".  Be careful, because
they may ask for transcripts later, or run a credit check on you also.

If you had courses in software design, System Analysis, or Database Design, GUI,
etc. you want to make sure they know that you have completed them and are eager
to learn new skills, and can work well in a team environment.  Just tell them
once and dont stress it too much, uless they want you to tell them something at
the end, like a recap of your experience.

Some companies prefer to hire someone that is fresh out of college and hasnt
learned any bad habbits yet.  If you worked for some place for the last 5 years
part time and stuck with it that could make a difference.  Often they pass over
people who have worked for 10 different companies for the last 20 years like the
Contract System Developers that just happen to be out of work, who will move on
the first time they have a good offer.

Don't sell yourself short and dont be surprised if they ask for qualifications
you don't have.  It is hard to find a good qualified employee.  You have to
sound confident, and intelligent.  Research the company on the internet if they
have a website and try to learn their jargon, what they do and what kind of an
image they have, what they sell, ect.  

Dont use Acronyms too much or abbreviations; the interviewer may be a human
resources individual that doesnt work in IT.  These types are more interested in
how intelligent you sound and how well you can carry on a conversation.  They
will ask you something like "Is there anything you want to ask us?", and you
should have a question or two on the tip of your tongue.  Maybe like work hours,
parking, or availability of housing like you expect to work for them, whether it
is a new position or a temporary one, etc.  Don't tell them you are the first
employer to offer you an interview or sound desperate.

If you have hobbies or do public service work or have outside interests
sometimes that is a plus if they ask about it.  Companies are always looking for
people to do volunteer work to make them look good.

They may be willing to offer you some rediculous starting wage as a trainee.
Experience is worth just as much as a big paycheck.

I think a telephone interview is often used to screen out prospective
applicants.  They may not ask too many questions, and they may ask a lot.  Out
of 50 applicants for a recent CICS job we scheduled 6 people for an in-person
interview.
```

Since you have zero years of experience they will be expecting to train

## Thread: runtime? — 17 msgs

### runtime?

- **From:** KNeddy@home.com
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T19:37:34+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS>`

```
Until I started researching  cobol and the net, I had never heard of
the term runtime.  So I'm a bit hazy on what this means exactly. I
always thought that when a cobol program was compiled, it was an
executable format and you could run it on what ever platform it was
developed.  One guy at work said that some compilers don't actually
create an executable, but create an intermediate file.  Is this the
reason why you have to have a cobol runtime installed on the server?
Do any of the compilers create an executable that doesn't require a
runtime to be installed on the server?  Any clarification on this
topic will be very helpful.
```

#### ↳ Re: runtime?

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald_tees@sympatico.ca>

- **Message-ID:** `<LEEE7.32808$6h5.2847781@news20.bellglobal.com>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS>`

```
The "runtime" is really the DLL librarys that generated code is dependent
on.  Every modern language is going to have some sort of library that must
be installed before the exe's will run.

#### ↳ Re: runtime?

- **From:** "Howard Brazee" <howard.brazee@cusys.edu>
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T22:00:15+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<PHEE7.1060$7x1.150776@bin4.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS>`

```
I guess there are two different definitions of "runtime".

I knew some applications need a runtime environment to run programs.  This
changes the cost structure.  I wasn't aware that there were CoBOL compilers
in this category.

The other definition concerns itself with called subprograms.  One option
when compiling a program is to pull in the sub program and compile it to
make a real efficient program.  If you change the subprogram, the calling
program doesn't change - this is a compile time call.

A different option is for the calling program to call the program at run
time.  If the sub program has been changed, that is the version called in.
```

#### ↳ Re: runtime?

- **From:** "JJ" <jj@nospam.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-03T00:16:38+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<GHGE7.528$2k1.194478@monger.newsread.com>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS>`

```
Some compilers compile to native code and others compile to psuedo-code
(p-code or byte code).  Some can do both.

With a p-code compiler, it compiles to a file that is interpreted by a
runtime interpreter, similar to Java.  Advantages are that the p-code object
file is usually much smaller than an executable file and can be portable to
any number of platforms.  For example, we use Acucobol and compile to
p-code.  We compile on a IBM AIX system, but our end users have a variety of
systems - Windows, HP-UX, Sun, SCO, Linux, DG, etc.  We don't need to own or
have access to any of those types of systems to do a port - we don't even
need to recompile.  We just order the proper runtime from Acucobol and our
p-code object files work on the desired platform.  (Acucobol does now have
an option to compile to native code on some platforms.)

Even if a compiler compiles to native code, it still may require a runtime
(for example, DLL files under Windows).  This would be similar to Visual
Basic - it compiles to native code, but still requires the VB runtime to be
installed on an end user system (a series of DLL files).  MS doesn't charge
for VB runtimes - don't know if any Cobol vendors who generate native code
charge for runtimes.

<KNeddy@home.com> wrote in message news:3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS...

##### ↳ ↳ Re: runtime?

- **From:** graham@olympic.co.uk (graham)
- **Date:** 2001-11-07T00:57:39-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8a02b0a1.0111070057.4bb9f465@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS> <D5CF7.13558$xS6.18045@www.newsranger.com>`

```
Thane Hubbell <nospam@newsranger.com> wrote in message news:<D5CF7.13558$xS6.18045@www.newsranger.com>...
> Runtime is not just a COBOL thing.  Look up MFC and Microsoft Visual C and C++
> - each requires a runtime.
> 
> 

Very, very, very true - it would be completely reasonable to consider
WINDOWS itself as a "runtime" for a whole lot of applications...

But on a more serious note..."runtime" packages are usually more
straightforward to work with insofar as the developer is more isolated
from the operating system than if they need to produce full .EXEs. As
mentioned elsewhere, the developer can just produce the intermediate
code modules, smack in the requisite "runtime" and evrything will just
work fine!!! (if only...).  With a .EXE there are often problems with
linking (which libraries to use, where are they etc.) and the
different operating systems and versions thereof often have different
linkage requirements. In theory the compiler writers do this work for
the developer when they create the appropriate runtime packages.

Probably, because COBOL has tended to be a cross-platform product,
most COBOL compilers has gone this way. On the other hand other
laguages, e.g. C/C++, are often (perhaps thinking of Microsoft here!)
produced with a specific target operating system in mind; in that case
they can rely on that environment to provide the "runtime" environment
without ever calling it a "runtime". Another well-known cross-platform
language has already been mentioned as having an intermediate code
type structure and a run-time: Java.

graham
Olympic Computers
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: runtime?

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-08T07:12:58+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BEA307A.A12B0A5C@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS> <D5CF7.13558$xS6.18045@www.newsranger.com> <8a02b0a1.0111070057.4bb9f465@posting.google.com>`

```
graham wrote:
> 
> Probably, because COBOL has tended to be a cross-platform product,
> most COBOL compilers has gone this way. 

You would take some work in convincing mainframers of this.  As far as
they are concerned their compilers produce hard code for their CPUs and
their compiler is 'most'.

> On the other hand other
> laguages, e.g. C/C++, are often (perhaps thinking of Microsoft here!)
> produced with a specific target operating system in mind; in that case
> they can rely on that environment to provide the "runtime" environment
> without ever calling it a "runtime". 

I am not sure that C or C++ are good examples of this.  They have
certainly been adopted by MS, but the approach to portabilty with C is
just different than that of other languages.  With C you just include
all the code with different requirements for various environments
(Operating Systems, word size, compilers) and head each with #if ...
#elsif.

> Another well-known cross-platform
> language has already been mentioned as having an intermediate code
> type structure and a run-time: Java.

One of the early languages for portability was Pascal with p-code
compilers available in the mid 70s.  Borland killed off that idea.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: runtime?

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2001-11-08T12:57:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<BivG7.79$0c7.45957@paloalto-snr1.gtei.net>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS> <D5CF7.13558$xS6.18045@www.newsranger.com> <8a02b0a1.0111070057.4bb9f465@posting.google.com> <3BEA307A.A12B0A5C@Azonic.co.nz> <3BEA3788.BC3C8BE3@sprynet.com>`

```
Frank Swarbrick <infocat@sprynet.com> wrote in message
news:3BEA3788.BC3C8BE3@sprynet.com...
>
> Hmm, IBM mainframe COBOL uses a runtime.  In fact, it now uses a
> multi-language runtime called Language Environment which is shared
> between COBOL, PL/I and C/C++.

This might be considered semantic nitpicking, but to say L/E is "shared" by
these language products is slightly inaccurate and understates Language
Environment.

L/E "exists." The three compilers mentioned generate object files which
"choose" to use the L/E runtime support. In addition, the L/E routines are
fully (I think) documented, and may be called explicitly from programs
written using any development product which has an external "CALL"
mechanism.

(Not that I don't think for a minute IBM didn't design L/E with at least one
explicit goal being the reduction of the number of 'compiler libraries' they
must maintain across their assorted language products).

In many ways, L/E on the mainframe is similar to Windows on a micro (PC) - a
bunch of useful functions with documented capabilities, serving as an
Applications Program Interface.

MCM
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ About LE (was: runtime?

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-08T13:43:09-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9sen94$2kl$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS> <D5CF7.13558$xS6.18045@www.newsranger.com> <8a02b0a1.0111070057.4bb9f465@posting.google.com> <3BEA307A.A12B0A5C@Azonic.co.nz> <3BEA3788.BC3C8BE3@sprynet.com> <BivG7.79$0c7.45957@paloalto-snr1.gtei.net>`

```
A few "clarifications" on LE (Language Environment)

1) Originally, it was a "separate" product, it is now "bundled" into the
operating system. If you have a current release of OS/390, z/OS, or VM fully
installed on your machine, then you also have LE installed.

2) As far as the Microsoft world goes, it is QUITE similar to the .NET
environment (i.e. it provides a "language independent" operating
environment)

3) There are two VERY different types of "modules" in LE
  A) Those that are well documented and explicitly CALLable by "application
programs" (these do things like date manipulation,  etc) - These routines
may be used by ANY supported LE programming language.
  B) those that ARE used by the compiler generated code, are named but not
documented, and provide functionality that COULD be included in the
generated code - but for various reasons are not.  These are specific to one
(or in some cases a few) programming languages.

4) There are "flavors" of LE for OS/390, z/OS, VM, VSE, and OS/400.  (the
status of OS/2 and/or Windows takes more time that I want to include in this
note).  This does provide IBM platform independence.

5) If you use ANY of the currently supported IBM COBOL, PL/I, C, or C++
compilers, you *must* have LE available at run-time or your object code will
"die a horrible death".

6) As far as COBOL goes, in "ye goode olde dayse" - there was a feature
"NORES" that allowed your object code to be "bundled" with its required
run-time support and then to run on a machine without any "run-time" support
programs.  That feature is REMOVED from the LE-enabled COBOL products.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: About LE (was: runtime?

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-09T17:09:20+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BEC0DC0.A6E4DEB9@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS> <D5CF7.13558$xS6.18045@www.newsranger.com> <8a02b0a1.0111070057.4bb9f465@posting.google.com> <3BEA307A.A12B0A5C@Azonic.co.nz> <3BEA3788.BC3C8BE3@sprynet.com> <BivG7.79$0c7.45957@paloalto-snr1.gtei.net> <9sen94$2kl$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
William M. Klein wrote:
> 
> A few "clarifications" on LE (Language Environment)
 
> 2) As far as the Microsoft world goes, it is QUITE similar to the .NET
> environment (i.e. it provides a "language independent" operating
> environment)

So does MS-DOS, or even CP/M <shrug>.

But .NET does go _much_ further, it also is, in principle, platform
independent.  In practice it is likely that MS will ensure that it is
only sufficiently independent to get a 'tick in the box', as it does
with much of its products.
 
> 4) There are "flavors" of LE for OS/390, z/OS, VM, VSE, and OS/400.  (the
> status of OS/2 and/or Windows takes more time that I want to include in this
> note).  This does provide IBM platform independence.

But not in the same way as was being discussed.  LE only provides the
same functionality on each platform, programs that are to run on these
different platforms must be recompiled for each of them using the
compilers for that platform, and possibly also _on_ that platform.  This
may lead to some changes being required in the source code.

UCSD, Java, AccuCobol, RM and MF can be compiled on one type of machine
and the resulting _compiled_ program distributed to completely different
_types_ of machine with different OSes.

> 6) As far as COBOL goes, in "ye goode olde dayse" - there was a feature
> "NORES" that allowed your object code to be "bundled" with its required
> run-time support and then to run on a machine without any "run-time" support
> programs.  That feature is REMOVED from the LE-enabled COBOL products.

What we (non-mainframers) would call statically linked.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: runtime?

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-09T06:47:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BEB7C18.E3F07417@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS> <D5CF7.13558$xS6.18045@www.newsranger.com> <8a02b0a1.0111070057.4bb9f465@posting.google.com> <3BEA307A.A12B0A5C@Azonic.co.nz> <3BEA3788.BC3C8BE3@sprynet.com>`

```
Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> 
> > > Probably, because COBOL has tended to be a cross-platform product,
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> between COBOL, PL/I and C/C++.

Which doesn't make it a 'cross-platform product', nor does it stop it
producing hard code for the CPU.

All high level language systems use libraries to provide generalised
routines for such areas as I-O and mathematical routines.  These
libraries can either be linked into the program statically or can be
accessed dynamically at 'runtime'.  The LE is a set of shared dynamic
libraries.

The 'runtime environment' of products such as RM, Accu, MF Cobols are
more like the Java VM in that a compiled program has no hard coded CPU
specific code in it and it can run on any platform (including an IBM
mainframe) that has a runtime environment (VM).  Other systems that have
been doing this for a quarter of a century or so have been: UCSD
(Pascal, Modula/2, Fortran), BOS (MicroCobol), Pick (Basic), more
recently Java, and now (or indeed any year 'soon') MS's .NET.
```

#### ↳ Re: runtime?

- **From:** Calvin Crumrine <Calvin_Crumrine@dced.state.ak.us>
- **Date:** 2001-11-07T10:44:06-09:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BE98F06.BDD29E0C@dced.state.ak.us>`
- **References:** `<3be2fd4a.20951519@NEWS>`

```
Assuming that your program is platform independent (e.g. doesn't make
any OS calls, etc.) then you can compile a program to dynamically link
to the runtime environment or compile it to statically link to the
runtime environment. (Basically this is compiling to intermediate code
or to a standalone EXE.) The main tradeoff is portability vs. size. If
you compile it to dynamically link to the runtime environment then you
can move the compiled program to another platform, install the
appropriate runtime environment for that platform, and your program will
still run. But if all your programs run on the same platform then you're
installing a lot more than you need (for one program) when you install
the runtime environment.

Using an older version (4) of MicroFocus COBOL Workbench as an example,
a program statically linked to the Windows runtime environment is
approximately 500KB larger than that program compiled for dynamic
linking to the runtime environment. I don't recall the minimum size of
the runtime environment, but 50MB sticks in my mind. Assuming that is
correct, it's more efficient (in terms of space usage) to statically
link your programs if you have fewer than 100 of them.

KNeddy@home.com wrote:

> Until I started researching  cobol and the net, I had never heard of
> the term runtime.  So I'm a bit hazy on what this means exactly. I
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> topic will be very helpful.
```

Mainly a salutary message for you younger whiz kids who think you've got
a handle on web applications.

My ISP concerned about home.com financial situation have sent three
messages suggesting their users sign up for a shaw.ca e-mail address. On
the third message, thought "Better get to it". Besides which the latest
message said it would only take 2 minutes !

Bring up their linked screen - Oops wants an ID (the one on the
bar-coded label on the Motorola box I have sat on the floor under my
L-shaped desk,  for direct cable connection). So get out of that screen,
get my aging body on my knees, and coupled with eye-glasses and
MAGNIFYING glass figure out the Serial # under the bar code.

Back to their screen :-

1 - enter your e-mail - Label next to it says "If your e-mail is
jjsmith.'@home.com', just enter 'jjsmith' - no big deal.

2. Enter that serial number above - OK

3. Enter your telephone number - OK - 403-271-2507

4. Enter password, repeat password. OK.

Press submit

Oops - doesn't like telephone number. OK, so Shaw is located in Calgary,
so they don't want my area code, so resubmit  with :-

        271-2507

Oops - doesn't like that. so resubmit with -

        271 2507

    2712507

This time it accepted the Telephone #. Would have been real nice if

spaces, NOT the Area code !"

OK - so I submit - no errors - but jumps me back to an empty submission
screen !

Contact Tech Support by phone - have you done "this' or 'that",  let's
check.......
All is kosher. "Well, I'll have to transfer you to a higher grade
tecchie.......". He does and I leave a message.

She gets back to me - "What did you key in ? What password did you use
?". Tell her. "Ah,  I see she says", but doesn't explain problem. "Let's
go to your Control Panel and enter it that route".

All honky dory. But the two minutes turned into 6 HOURS !

IMPORTANT - how come this particular piece of software was released for

Jimmy, Calgary AB

## Thread: netexpress 3.1 Abort of a program without any notice — 2 msgs

### netexpress 3.1 Abort of a program without any notice

- **From:** Marion.Johann.Vry@nord-com.net (Johann Vry)
- **Date:** 2001-11-02T12:53:52-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b359c685.0111021253.2a55a3be@posting.google.com>`

```
What could be the reason for an abort of netexpress-programs without
any notice on the screen?

The abord could occurs for example three times an hour at different
situations.
```

#### ↳ Re: netexpress 3.1 Abort of a program without any notice

- **From:** graham@olympic.co.uk (graham)
- **Date:** 2001-11-07T01:04:47-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8a02b0a1.0111070104.698396cb@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<b359c685.0111021253.2a55a3be@posting.google.com>`

```
Sorry - but you really will have to give more details...

I certainly have seen things like this - usually some run-time error
but in an environment where there is nowhere for the application to
display the message. The application is probably encountering a fatal
error, the program is not trapping the error and thus not reporting it
to the user itself, the COBOL environment would send some sort of
message (often an information window) but in the particular
circumstances this fails, and then the whole thing terminates.

1) is this your program?
2) where (i.e. the developer's or the user's machine) is it failing?
3) is it reproducible?
3) can you (or have you at any time in the past) use(d) Animator to
investigate it?

graham
Olympic Computers

Marion.Johann.Vry@nord-com.net (Johann Vry) wrote in message news:<b359c685.0111021253.2a55a3be@posting.google.com>...

## Thread: COBOL on the Web....HELP! — 4 this month / 23 total

_Topics: [`Web, XML, modern integration`](topics.md#web)_

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL on the Web....HELP!

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-03T17:29:30+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BE4297A.6BF29C6F@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3bde0281.647438122@NEWS> <bcfdd616.0110292251.53ef1a6f@posting.google.com> <3bde596d.4008691@NEWS>`

```
kneddy@home.com wrote:
> I want to write a script in COBOL that updates files.  I want to
> create a web page on the internet, have the user fill out a form, and
> then when the submit button is clicked, execute a script written in
> COBOL.  Why COBOL you ask.  Simply because I don't know Java or Perl
> but I do know how to code the heck out of COBOL.  

You could try CobolScript.  It is mostly like Cobol, but is scripting
like Perl or Python, costs only $US 50.00 for the professional version,
has CGI interface (and ftp and EMail), can access SQL (but not ISAM
files), has Windows and Linux (and BSD and Sun) versions, and can build
standalone executables with no runtime cost (unless you are an ISP or
ASP provider).

see http://www.cobolscript.com
```

- **From:** "Acucorp News" <shaun_gough@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-26T15:59:33-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1451C740A890D411B65C00104B95B1C04A2755@ras.acucorp.com>`
- **References:** `<3bde0281.647438122@NEWS> <bcfdd616.0110292251.53ef1a6f@posting.google.com> <YmJG7.46216$zK1.11995906@typhoon.tampabay.rr.com> <b5yM7.84$kY4.2174@dfw-service2.ext.raytheon.com>`

```
I am not sure if this is possible in other COBOLs, but Acucorp does have
some good Documentation and Examples in the standard Development System that
you can purchase, explaining exactly how you can have a HTML form to obtain
data and send it to COBOL for processing, as with any other COBOL
application.

Acucorp also has a Web Plugin, so that you can execute COBOL applications
directly from an Internet Browser, so depending on how you want the
application to look and feel, depends on which route you want to take.

Please take a look at the Acucorp Website, and do not hesitate to contact me
directly if you ahev any questions.
```

#### ↳ Re: database software for Fujitsu Cobol

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-07T11:08:16+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3be85fc0_5@news.newsgroups.com>`
- **References:** `<3be74cce.385509581@NEWS>`

```
Jerry already mentioned that just about anything will "interface" to
Fujitsu.

You need to understand what ODBC is. IF you have a driver for ODBC and
configure it on your server or system, your Fujitsu COBOL can interface to
ANY relational Database that the ODBC driver supports.

Start with ACCESS. It is simple and a full RDB implementation. If you have
access installed you will already have the ODBC driver for it.

Some advice...

1. Start with some simple SQL embedded in your COBOL. You will need the
Fujitsu RTS configuration file set up to point at your database. (ODBCinfo).
Read the Manual.

2. Use the RDB PURELY as a receptacle for data. Drive it from your COBOL
program with embedded SQL. Do NOT USE RDB specific features like DB
Procedures on the database.

If this means nothing to you, mail me privately.

Pete.


<kneddy@home.com> wrote in message news:3be74cce.385509581@NEWS...
> We are looking for some database software that will interface with
> Fujitsu Cobol....any recommendations?
>
>

>  I appreciate the info.  Are there any books you could recommend?

>
Structured Query Language (SQL) has 7 or 8 basic "Commands" and is designed
to be easy to learn. Nevertheless, it is extremely powerful. (part of this
power comes from the fact that it is "Structured" and commands can be
"nested" inside each other, but that is more advanced usage...).

Do a Web Search for tutorials on it (Google gives at least a dozen...) I
have referred students to some of these sites and they picked it up very
quickly.

The best books are anything by Codd or Date (they developed the Relational
Model) but these are usually way beyond a beginner and a bit of an
"overkill" if you just want to manage a RDB from COBOL.

I am sending  you a paper I wrote on accessing Relational Data Bases from
COBOL. It is intended as a primer for people who have never done it before
and are not familiar with the environment. It contains sample code. This
paper has proved helpful in the past to many students.

HTH,

Pete.

I was on my feet during the last 300 metres... It was an ethereal experience
all right... <G>

I had Ethereal in a quinella with Freemason but certainly never picked it as
a winner...

Really a cosmopolitan effort; NZ horse, trained in NZ by a pommie sheila,
ridden by an Aussie jockey who was very modest regarding his contribution...

Never mind, you beat us at everything else, and now the cricket's starting
again... I guess all we can console ourselves with are the Melbourne and
America's Cups...

> Trying to contact you privately is unsuccessful - your server is unknown.
Is
> it me?

No, it isn't you. But neither am I trying to hide. The trouble is that as
soon as you post anything to a Newsgroup, the web crawling 'bots are all
over it and the next thing you know you are deluged with spam...

As I don't need Viagra (well, not this week anyway...<G>), am not interested
in MLM, already support all the charities I am ever going to, and am NOT a
sucker for a sob story about some abused child who needs a heart transplant
if I will just forward the mail... it becomes essential to do SOMETHING that
will confuse the 'bots.

I therefore insert the word "nospam" into the e-mail address I use for this
NG, so it becomes: dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz

Now, a 'bot is unlikely to be programmed to recognise this word "nospam", as
most of them simply search for the @ sign and grab the text surrounding
it.... The address goes onto a mailing list and is eventually sold for
serious money. Problem is that any mail sent to it is returned as
undeliverable... This tends to make for dissatisfied customers who bought
the spammers mailing list. Especially if many people have done as I did...

And that, in my opinion, is a consummation devoutly to be wished...<G> (or,
if you're not into Shakespeare,..."Serve the bastards right!")

Obviously, spammers reading this will be already modifying their 'bots to
handle the "nospam", but it doesn't matter. I can just change it to any
combination of characters that will make my address invalid. The
possibilities are almost limitless....

On the other hand, a Human, being possessed of more intelligence than a Web
Crawling Robot, can look at my e-mail address and REMOVE the word
"nospam"... (well once it has been pointed out to them, they can <G>).

And that's what you need to do. (Actually, you don't, because I will be
sending you the requested material privately and this will come from a
completely different e-mail address reserved for that purpose.)

HTH,

Pete.

You may use Pervasive/Btrieve. That way you don't have to learn SQL or

benefit of transaction control).

Manny Apalisok

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<caa2756a.0111082150.7b62b411@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<3be74cce.385509581@NEWS> <caa2756a.0111072249.58db6d8a@posting.google.com> <9sf1nn$1cdi$1@otis.netspace.net.au>`

```
"> Does use of Pervasive/Btrieve tie you into a particular operating
platform?

I believe the latest version at least supports Netware, NT, and Linux.

> How widely is it distributed? Personally, I've never heard of it, but that
> may be just my problem.
> 

If you came from mainframe, it's unknown. But I think Btrieve was the
database engine for Novell's Netware, so if you used Novell before
then you may have come across it without knowing. But better check it
at www.pervasive.com.

The nice thing about it, accordingly, is (if I still get my cobol
syntax right) you just change the assignment like:

SELECT FILEA ASSIGN TO "FILEA.DAT"

to

SELECT FILEA ASSIGN TO "FILEA.DAT, BTRV"

where the keyword BTRV (if it's correct) identifies the file as
Btrieve.
(This was true about 3 years ago. Not sure if it still is today).

Manny Apalisok
```

## Thread: excel from cobol — 10 msgs

### excel from cobol

- **From:** im4liberty@aol.com (Im4Liberty)
- **Date:** 2001-11-06T02:57:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20011105215718.03573.00001375@mb-mw.aol.com>`

```
Hello,

Has anyone ever successfully updated an excel spreadsheet from a NetExpress
COBOL program?   I've been able to "connect" to the spreadsheet via ODBC, but
I'm not sure how to get data into the cells.   INSERT/UPDATE commands don't
seem to work, as I'm not sure what the "table" name is (I tried using "sheet1"
to no avail).   Is there a way to update the 'sheet directly, without going
through ODBC?

Any input would be appreciated.

Bill
```

#### ↳ Re: excel from cobol

- **From:** pvieira@emporsoft.pt (Paulo Vieira)
- **Date:** 2001-11-06T01:34:50-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b5b8d7c7.0111060134.2631539c@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<20011105215718.03573.00001375@mb-mw.aol.com>`

```
im4liberty@aol.com (Im4Liberty) wrote in message news:<20011105215718.03573.00001375@mb-mw.aol.com>...
> Hello,
> 
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> Bill

Hello Bill
Yes there is a much simpler way. I haven't done it in NetExpress, but
with Fujitsu; but I'm shure since Microfocus is able to invoke OLE
objects, that it is not a problem.
First thing you must know is the OLE name of Excel:
"excel.application".
In Fujitsu we have a special class to handle OLE comunication, so a
write:
INVOKE OLE "CREATE-OBJECT" USING APP-NAME RETURNING OLE-HANDLE
where:
-OLE is my special class for OLE objects 
-APP-NAME is a PIC X(17) value "excel.application"
-OLE-HANDLE is an OBJECT REFERENCE OF CLASS OLE

After you have established a handle to Excel, there is a LOT of things
you can do:
Open Workbooks, open specific spreadsheets in a workbook, GET and SET
values for a cell or range of cells, etc.. That, of course, you'll
have to learn from the Microsoft Documentation.
By the way, if you happen to go this way, don't follow Microsoft
examples for VB, since there you can have something like:
   app-name.Workbook(dumb.xls).sheet(sheet1).range(A2).value = val
that, in COBOL, translate to 7 calls
   invoke OLE "CREATE-OBJECT" using app-nm returning excel
   invoke excel "GET-Workbooks" returning Workbook
   invoke Workbook "Open" using fileName UpdateLinks returning
workbook
   invoke workbook "GET-worksheets" returning sheets
   invoke sheets "GET-Item" using sheetName returning worksheet
and then
   move 2 to arrayRow
   move 1 to arrayCol
   invoke worksheet "GET-cells" using arrayRow arrayCol returning cell
   invoke cell "SET-Value" using val

and so on

regards, 
Paulo
```

#### ↳ Re: excel from cobol

<a id="t-ccfa98c8ef"></a>
## Thread: COBOL and C/C++ — 7 msgs

### COBOL and C/C++

- **From:** "Matthias Philipp" <wrongmail@web.de>
- **Date:** 2001-11-06T12:10:08+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9s8g7h$11cei2$1@ID-109843.news.dfncis.de>`

```
Hello out there!
I'm a COBOL-Newbie and I have to read a COBOL-Data-File with C/C++. Are
there any includes for C for that job?
I wonder if there is any possibility to read a cobol-structure into a
c-struct.
thanks for any help!

Matthias
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL and C/C++

- **From:** "JerryP" <news@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-06T13:06:40+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<AfRF7.75165$tb2.6004396@bin2.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<9s8g7h$11cei2$1@ID-109843.news.dfncis.de>`

```
There is no such thing as a "COBOL-Data-File."

1. COBOL can write standard sequential text files.
2. COBOL can write files in organizational formats proprietary (=secret) to
the compiler in use.
3. COBOL can access standard database formats (BTrieve, Access, Excel,
etc.).

If #1 or #3, you're golden.

If #2, you still have two choices: A) Write a COBOL program to read the file
under investigation and output the file in some (text?) format you can
access, or B) Use - with varying degrees of effort and success - third party
conversion routines.

If, for example, you have a production COBOL ISAM file that you want to
fiddle with using C, (keeping the original file and file structure), you
have a career.

I could be out of date on the above, but I firmly believe it's turtles all
the way down.


"Matthias Philipp" <wrongmail@web.de> wrote in message
news:9s8g7h$11cei2$1@ID-109843.news.dfncis.de...
> Hello out there!
> I'm a COBOL-Newbie and I have to read a COBOL-Data-File with C/C++. Are
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL and C/C++

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-09T06:53:26+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BEB7D66.7FBA2CC3@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<9s8g7h$11cei2$1@ID-109843.news.dfncis.de> <AfRF7.75165$tb2.6004396@bin2.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
JerryP wrote:
> 
> If, for example, you have a production COBOL ISAM file that you want to
> fiddle with using C, (keeping the original file and file structure), you
> have a career.

Microfocus provided a callable routine for its file handler and this can
be called by C programs.  As it is the actual file handler it maintains
the integrity of the Cobol file even when concurrently accessing with
Cobol or other C programs.

Of course you still need to know the format of the data and ensure that
the record fields are not corrupted.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL and C/C++

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2001-11-06T13:19:28+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ArRF7.289$ea5.74175@paloalto-snr1.gtei.net>`
- **References:** `<9s8g7h$11cei2$1@ID-109843.news.dfncis.de>`

```
http://www.flexus.com/downloads.html
Get file COBDATA.ZIP; this is a tutorial on COBOL data types.

You will also find http://www.flexus.com/ebd2asc.html useful; it addresses
the question, "How can I convert COBOL-created data for use in my BASIC,
C/C++ or other non-COBOL programs, and what about EBCDIC-ASCII
considerations?"

If you are looking for something where you can just call a DLL to convert
data on the fly, I have a freeware DLL you may use for non-commercial
purposes (I explain what that means). You will get a questionnaire to
answer; but that you are a programmer, but not a COBOL programmer (well, a
"newbie" by your own standards) means you are exactly the target audience
for whom I developed this conversion software.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL and C/C++

- **From:** Daniel Jacot<daniel.jacot@winterthur.ch>
- **Date:** 2001-11-07T15:55:38+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<_PcG7.16072$xS6.23680@www.newsranger.com>`
- **References:** `<9s8g7h$11cei2$1@ID-109843.news.dfncis.de>`

```

On Tue, 6 Nov 2001 12:10:08 +0100, in article
<9s8g7h$11cei2$1@ID-109843.news.dfncis.de>, Matthias Philipp stated...
>
>Hello out there!
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>

As usual, the best answer is 'it depends '.

It depends on the operating system, the file-organisation and the code page of
the file  (ASCII, EBCDIC).
It depends on the COBOL datatypes you use. There is no direct equivalent to the
COBOL COMP-3 (packed-decimal), nor to numeric picture items in C. Strings are
not '\0' terminated but either fixed or variable in length.
It depends on the COBOL compiler you used to produce the file.
It depends on the C/C++ compiler you want to use to read the file.

Please post the COBOL structure and give us  the  informations  mentioned above.
Post the C/C++ code you have written so far. Post the problems you encountered
so far.  Maybe we are willing to help you then. Maybe we will ask you to RTFM.

-------------------------------------------------
With kind regards
Daniel Jacot
-------------------------------------------------
visit us at: http://www.winterthur.com
```

### COBOL FAQ

- **From:** wmklein@ix.netcom.com (William M. Klein)
- **Date:** 2001-11-06T12:26:10+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol,news.answers,comp.answers,alt.answers
- **Message-ID:** `<computer-lang/cobol-faq_1005049521@rtfm.mit.edu>`

```
Archive-name: computer-lang/cobol-faq
Posting-Frequency: twice a month
Last-Modified: 2000/07/02
Version: 3.01
URL: http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm
Reply-To: wmklein@ix.netcom.com


                            COBOL FAQ
                  (Frequently Asked Questions)

Last-Modified: Sunday, July 2, 2000

The COBOL FAQ has moved.  To view the most recent version, please check out the
web version at:

  http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm

If you have comments, corrects, deletions, or additions, please send private
email to:

    wmklein <at> ix.netcom.com

The following is Appendix B.5 - Changes to create Version 3.01

 o Recorded new location of the FAQ
 o Updated some old (bad) web links
 o Added some new COBOL books (particularly those written or contributed to - by
frequent comp.lang.cobol submitters).
 o Added information about LegacyJ (PERCobol) and changed the company name from
"Synkronix" to "LegacyJ".
 o Updated information for changes in product and company names and addresses
where available
 o Updated the URLs for downloading the draft of the next COBOL Standard and
CobCy
 o Started the Samples/Example Section
 o Tried to get rid of most specific references to Windows/NT, Windows/95,
Windows/98, and Windows/2000.
 o Added links to Xinotech
 o Added information on Norcom and GUI ScreenIO
 o Added (back) information on Wang
 o Added (back) information on the Tiny-COBOL ('74 Standard) project
```

## Thread: MicroFocus COBOL ISAM files - are they C/ISAM compatible? — 7 this month / 9 total

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files)_

### MicroFocus COBOL ISAM files - are they C/ISAM compatible?

- **From:** "Tzachi Nissim" <tzachi@attunity.co.il>
- **Date:** 2001-11-07T11:45:33+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9savsh$hkg$1@news.netvision.net.il>`

```
Hi,

We are trying to access files created using Micro Focus COBOL on an HP
machine using a CISAM ODBC with partial success. Most files work okay. It
looks like the variable length files are not working.

Does anyone know if MicroFocus COBOL produces CISAM compatible files? If
so - which version of CISAM?

Any help would be appreciated...

Tzachi
```

#### ↳ Re: MicroFocus COBOL ISAM files - are they C/ISAM compatible?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-07T15:30:26-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9sc95o$ug6$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<9savsh$hkg$1@news.netvision.net.il>`

```
1) "Traditionally" Micro Focus COBOL under HP is a "weird" combination of
Micro Focus and HP technology.  Therefore, what is true of Micro Focus COBOL
in other environments is SOMETIMES not true under HP.

2) "normal" Micro Focus *does* have an OPTION to produce C-ISAM files.

What I would suggest you do is check YOUR compiler documentation (probably
the "User Guide") for the FILE-TYPE directive - and see what it says about
C-ISAM
```

breaks that assumption.

although they reside in the same COBOL file. As you probably have some
kind of flag indicating the type of record, that is of good candidate
for an 88 level.
