#### ↳ Re: Cobol & PL/1

- **From:** theodp@aol.com (Theo DP)
- **Date:** 2001-11-11T16:41:34+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20011111114134.27244.00004908@mb-mq.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<1s_G7.115814$B72.30976955@news1.rdc1.az.home.com>`

```
>Subject: Cobol & PL/1
>From: "Rufio" davecawdell@home.com 
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
>

No offense to you, but it still amazes me how casually IT management takes the
issue of knowledge these days on the mainframe and other platforms.

Indeed, many shops see no need to at all to have any employees that understand
the languages used in their mission-critical systems.

Regarding PL/I, it can be quite different than COBOL, since it lacks some
useful features you may be used to using with COBOL (e.g., SEARCH, SORT, GROUP
moves, etc.) and introduces some other concepts and features that many COBOL
programmers have never seen (i.e., internal user-defined functions, recursion,
dynamic allocation of variables, multitasking, etc.).

As far as obvious mistakes, try to at least avoid the one that a former
employer of mine made. 

After assigning a PL/I system to a COBOL programmer who was also learning "on
the fly", I got an angry call from the department head who was upset that the
system would no longer run at all.

He went on to note that the only changes the new programmer made had only "made
things much better" by renumbering and reordering all the routines to make it
look like the COBOL programs, blissfully unaware of the repercussions of
rescoping all of the variables and subroutines.

:-}
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol & PL/1

- **From:** Daniel Jacot<daniel.jacot@winterthur.ch>
- **Date:** 2001-11-12T08:57:10+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<G9MH7.21433$xS6.32842@www.newsranger.com>`
- **References:** `<1s_G7.115814$B72.30976955@news1.rdc1.az.home.com>`

```
Obvious mistakes? There are a couple of problems, some of them might be:

- STATIC and AUTOMATIC variables behave different when entering a procedure.
- Pl/I stuctures are ALIGNED by default while COBOL structures are not SYNC. The
two languages insert their padding bytes in a defferent manner.
- You may CALL a COBOL program from PL/I without any problem, but not
vice-versa. You have to read carefully the ILC manual if  mix both languages.
- Be aware of the scope of names in PL/I.
- There are many defaults in PL/I. You may even use variables which have no
declaration and therefore they are declared implicitly by the compiler
accordeing to the first letter of their name.
- There are no reserved keywords in PL/I as are in COBOL. Whether a word in the
source is a variable or a program control atatement is determined by the
compiler. IF IF = THEN THEN THEN = IF * 2; is a perfectly valid statement.
- There are no 'verbs' in PL/I like 'MOVE', 'COMPUTE' or 'STRING'. There are
statements which end with a semicolon and blocks which end with an 'END;'
statement.
- Addresses are much more appreciated in PL/I than in COBOL. You'll find PTR and
BASED everywhere in PL/I sources
- Arithmetic operations in PL/I often end with FOFL conditions while COBOL
handles most of this type of error.

Conclusion: You might need to RTFM and/or need assistance by an experienced PL/I
programmer.

On Sat, 10 Nov 2001 00:23:25 GMT, in article
<1s_G7.115814$B72.30976955@news1.rdc1.az.home.com>, Rufio stated...
>
>I'm starting a new contract next week, and will be working on an MVS
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>

-------------------------------------------------
With kind regards
Daniel Jacot
-------------------------------------------------
visit us at: http://www.winterthur.com
```

Rudy

##### ↳ ↳ Re: animator in unix...... can not get access to ALT and CRTL keys

- **From:** rudyten@yahoo.com (Rudy)
- **Date:** 2001-11-16T17:03:53-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b9be6b58.0111161703.383433e2@posting.google.com>`

GOT IT FIXED....
All I did was create a file called "ADISKEY.MAP" and placed it on my
directory.
The content of the file was as follows:
------------------------
Meta-Char is "/"
-----------------------
that is right......just in line of text. 
Hope this helps if anyone else runs into this problem. Found the
answer in "COBOL V4.0 for UNIX    System Reference - Voulume 2" page
O-4.
```

### Problem with compiler COBOL SET FOR AIX

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Identifying a "TAB" Character in an ASCII file using COBOL

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald_tees@sympatico.ca>
- **Date:** 2001-11-12T20:01:24-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ga_H7.7408$vR4.1129715@news20.bellglobal.com>`
- **References:** `<kmWH7.2046$Eq.224940@news.xtra.co.nz> <3BF0361F.2736BD14@shaw.ca> <3BF05F3D.9534A550@shaw.ca>`

```
That will not work, Jimmy.  If he is going to replace the TAB with anything,
it has to be a character not likely to be used in a character string. I tend
to use the TILDE for that sort of thing, but I write pretty simple systems
for one language.

However, I do not think that the problem.  The problem is, as Thane said,
that a LINE SEQUENTIAL file is one of those funny little cobol things that
really means "whatever your system regards as text" or maybe "source code
format".  It is system dependent, and on a PC usually has tabs expanded to
spaces at an invisible level.  There may be a switch that can be set to stop
that, I do not know.

There are several ways you can take care of the problem. I would create a
file object that mimics the behaviour of the file type I wanted
wanted(unexpanded tabs), and use the "UNSTRING DELIMITED BY ALL x'09'."
method, just as the code is written. The actual code in the object could
read the file one byte at a time, sequentially.  That way you will see
everything, character by character, including whatever your system uses for
an end of line (PC <CR><LF>). While it would be system dependent, you could
easily put in a platform PROPERTY that allowed you to set the local file
type.  That could be stored in the local setup object.

For that matter, the whole LINE-SEQUENTIAL file structure could be packed
into a standard FILE-OBJECT that had PROPERTIES settable at runtime instead
of OPTIONS set at compile time. That is the sort of thing that object cobol
standards should set.  I'd be willing to bet money that the runtime
libraries already contain code to do both, and check a flag at runtime
anyway. But that is a whole other topic. (or is it?)

Donald.

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Identifying a "TAB" Character in an ASCII file using COBOL

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T17:57:13+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BF15EF9.D98B1B8F@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<kmWH7.2046$Eq.224940@news.xtra.co.nz> <3BF0361F.2736BD14@shaw.ca>`

```
James J. Gavan wrote:
> 
> greg wrote:
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> If  mystring(1:22) =  x"09"

No, that is not the problem at all.

When a LINE SEQUENTIAL file is read the TAB characters in the record are
exapnded to a number of spaces by the READ statement.  This means that
the TAB characters are not there to be tested against x"09", or any
other value.

There is no mechanism to avoid this TAB expansion on reading with a LINE
SEQUENTIAL file.

The best solution is to get the extract file in comma-separated format. 
If this is not possible then you may need to read the file as RECORD
SEQUENTIAL (ie SEQUENTIAL).  This imposes fixed length and ignores the
CR/LF terminators, but doesn't expand TABs.

Option 1:

   Make the record size 1 byte and read until CR/LF or EOF building the
line in memory.

   This is very slow.  

Option 2:     

    Make the record size 128 (or so) and extract records into W-S, each
time the end of the record is reached read another.

    You will get a 9/18 error on the last record but you can extract
from it anyway.  As a precaution move spaces to the record area before
each read.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Identifying a "TAB" Character in an ASCII file using COBOL

line sequential or line advancing files during a READ operation, into the
equivalent number of spaces."

At

http://support.merant.com/websupport/docs/microfocus/books/nx31books/fhpubb0
3.htm

 "Chapter 6: File Handler Configuration"

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-12T23:36:53-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9sqbsm$9g1$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<kmWH7.2046$Eq.224940@news.xtra.co.nz> <3BF0361F.2736BD14@shaw.ca> <3BF15EF9.D98B1B8F@Azonic.co.nz> <9sqbbm$2u9$1@slb3.atl.mindspring.net>`

Ok,  I just found it.
  In addition to the EXPANDTAB feature listed below, check your user manual
for the
         T
 run-time switch.  I think this will do exactly what you want (i.e. leave
TAB characters as they are and not convert them to spaces).
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Identifying a "TAB" Character in an ASCII file using COBOL

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T09:12:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BF23572.3DD65B85@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<kmWH7.2046$Eq.224940@news.xtra.co.nz> <3BF0361F.2736BD14@shaw.ca> <3BF15EF9.D98B1B8F@Azonic.co.nz>`

```
> > greg wrote:
> >
> > > We are trying to import a TAB separated variable file using Microsoft COBOL
> > > version 5.0 

William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com> wrote:
> Ok,  I just found it.
>   In addition to the EXPANDTAB feature listed below, 

Unfortunately it is not NetExpress that greg is using, it is MS Cobol
5.0, equivalent to MF Cobol 3.0.  There is no EXPANDTAB.

> check your user manual for the
>          T
>  run-time switch.  I think this will do exactly what you want (i.e. leave
> TAB characters as they are and not convert them to spaces).

The T switch only applies to outputting tabs into the file on writing.

To quote from the MS Cobol 5.0 manual: "On input, tab characters are
expanded to spaces to the next position REGARDLESS of the setting of the
T switch."

That's 2 for 2    ;-)
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Identifying a "TAB" Character in an ASCII file using COBOL

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T14:42:47-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9ss0oj$iau$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<kmWH7.2046$Eq.224940@news.xtra.co.nz> <3BF0361F.2736BD14@shaw.ca> <3BF15EF9.D98B1B8F@Azonic.co.nz> <3BF23572.3DD65B85@Azonic.co.nz>`

```
As I indicated in my note, the user should check THEIR manual.  However, I
have a "vague" memory that the T run-time switch *did* impact tabs on a READ
by the time of Microsoft V5.  Have you tried it and found that it does NOT
work?

The obvious solution is to upgrade to a currently supported COBOL product -
if the one from the early '90s doesn't provide the functionality the user is
looking for. The original note said,

"Is there a work around short of using another language/upgraded version?"

So far, I haven't seen one - but maybe there is one somewhere (short of
checking to see if the T run-time switch DOES work and/or if the EXPANDTAB
feature is ALSO documented in the MS V5 product)
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Identifying a "TAB" Character in an ASCII file using COBOL

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T14:18:49+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BF27D49.C277C5A9@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<kmWH7.2046$Eq.224940@news.xtra.co.nz> <3BF0361F.2736BD14@shaw.ca> <3BF15EF9.D98B1B8F@Azonic.co.nz> <3BF23572.3DD65B85@Azonic.co.nz> <9ss0oj$iau$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
William M. Klein wrote:
> 
> As I indicated in my note, the user should check THEIR manual. 

As I quoted directly from a copy of the same MS Cobol 5.0 manual, I
don't see how their manual would be any different from this.

>  However, I
> have a "vague" memory that the T run-time switch *did* impact tabs on a READ
> by the time of Microsoft V5.  Have you tried it and found that it does NOT
> work?

Yes, I have tried it with MS Cobol 5.0.  The products works exactly as
described in the manual, even using the CALL x"91" functions to change
the T switch internally has no effect on reading (as expected).  Your
vague memory is incorrect.  This action of the T switch, and tab
expansion on reading, has been consistent since at least Level II Cobol
2.5, with which I first noticed this problem, through to Object Cobol
4.1.  The earlier CIS Cobol didn't have a T switch, and probably didn't
output tabs.

Here is a quote cut and pasted from the HTML Object-Cobol 4.1 manual:

"On input, tab characters are always expanded to spaces to the next
position, regardless of the setting of the T switch."
 
> The obvious solution is to upgrade to a currently supported COBOL product -
> if the one from the early '90s doesn't provide the functionality the user is
> looking for. The original note said,
> 
> "Is there a work around short of using another language/upgraded version?"

Your 'obvious solution' is directly opposed to the required solution,
and thus is not a solution.

> So far, I haven't seen one 

Strange that, I posted _two_ work arounds in the message that you
replied to: 1) re-extract data with comma-separated data, or 2) use
sequential file and build the lines from single bytes or fixed blocks. 
Both of which: a) _will_ work, and b) are infinitely quicker and cheaper
than buying NetExpress 

NetExpress may also require a new machine to run it on.  MS Cobol 5.0
_may_ be being used under DOS or Windows 3.11, or may be running in a
DOS emulator.

> - but maybe there is one somewhere (short of
> checking to see if the T run-time switch DOES work 

It doesn't, it works exactly as the manual says.  The MF Cobol manuals
also have the exact same wording.  What does your manual say ?

> and/or if the EXPANDTAB
> feature is ALSO documented in the MS V5 product)

It isn't (as I had already told you).  Not only that, but the compiler
rejects the EXPANDTAB and NOEXPANDTAB directives if it is fed to them.
```

- **Message-ID:** `<9ssnel$7d$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
"Richard Plinston" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote in message
news:3BF27D49.C277C5A9@Azonic.co.nz...
> William M. Klein wrote:
> >
>
> It isn't (as I had already told you).  Not only that, but the compiler
> rejects the EXPANDTAB and NOEXPANDTAB directives if it is fed to them.

EXPANDTAB is never a directive, it is an EXTFH feature. See my previous
reference to:

http://support.merant.com/websupport/docs/microfocus/books/nx31books/fhpubb0
3.htm
Topic,
   "6.2 Configuration Options"


For anyone with a currently supported Micro Focus (MERANT) product (who is
also interested in handling tabs in line sequential input files), here is
what the online documentation says about the T run-time switch at:

http://support.merant.com/websupport/docs/microfocus/books/nx31books/lrpubb1
9.htm

under the topic
 "15.1.2 The READ Statement"
subtopic,
  Directives and Run-time Switches

"T - controls the interpretation of tab characters when reading line
sequential records."
```

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-12T17:19:32-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9spllu$ie5$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<kmWH7.2046$Eq.224940@news.xtra.co.nz> <6HWH7.22174$xS6.34722@www.newsranger.com> <S3YH7.28256$Wa.2322121@bin1.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <YJYH7.22333$xS6.34820@www.newsranger.com>`

As I recall, there is a run-time switch that controls whether or not tabs
are expanded in LINE SEQUENTIAL files.  If the "input file" has records
delimited by CR/LF, then you certainly would want to define it as LINE
SEQUENTIAL.  Therefore, I would check the Micro Focus documentation for
run-time switches that determine the processing of TABS - in data fields.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: What is COBOL done on?

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald_tees@sympatico.ca>
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T10:47:29-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<RewI7.17075$vR4.2312860@news20.bellglobal.com>`
- **References:** `<3BF0B906.597F507F@Uni.com> <3BF11ECF.B59F86A@neo.rr.com> <7l9I7.40630$XR.2861623@bin3.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <a50fcf68.0111131615.6dc62d6d@posting.google.com> <3BF27EFE.F526C206@Azonic.co.nz> <2IvI7.54335$Wa.3702688@bin1.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
"JerryP" <news@bisusa.com> wrote in message
news:2IvI7.54335$Wa.3702688@bin1.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com...
>
> "Richard Plinston" <riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote in message
…[20 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I think you quite wrong.  The discussion is about programming, and neither
bi-metallic strips nor light switches require software yet.

However, imbedded computers such as those used in cars DO require
programming, and certainly account for a sizable percentage of programmer
occupations. They are not simple logic chips, they are full-bore
stored-program Von Neuman machines, ... with storage devices and lots of
interfacing.  I've spent a sizable proportion of my carreer programming such
computers, and, in fact, got my first PC for precisely that purpose ... as a
software development platform.

Interestingly enough, one of the first of those computers (the mostek F8)
had an assembler that was written in Cobol.  It ran on a PDP-10, and
produced tapes for a PROM blaster.  I, personally, had about 10,000 of those
systems running, and could not have done it without Cobol.

As I see the future, a very large percentage of those computers are going to
behave as a very intelligent device, hooked into a larger program through an
OCX control and either an ethernet or USB/firewire style of interface.
Systems for controling things like building heat and lights will be built
from both hardware and software components that behave like "objects".

Cobol is one of the few fairly high level languages that is designed for
system integration.  To limit the discussion to computers that are only used
as destop, standalone machines is very short sighted.  In fact, that the
language runs on main frames through to micro's is the the most important
aspect of the language.  It is the ONLY language with a standardized mass
storage interface that encompasses such a large variety of hardware, and the
ONLY language with built in multi-language support.

Donald.
```

You can build a multi-human-language library in any computer language,
obviously. Cobol, however, has had multi alphabet support for at least ten
years, for example.  There is a pretty huge difference between changing one
statement at the start of a program to deterime alphabet than there is to
using one of several different sets of source code and libraries. The amount
of work you did would likely double if you had to code all that as well.

 I will, however, modify my statement, as I obviously am not familiar with
every computer language in existence.  It is the only one of the major
general purpose languages with built in language support.  I was not really
considering languages such as HTML, or JAVA.  Those are both primarilly net
interface languages, and obviously have support for multiple languages. If
an application has nothing to do with the internet, I doubt you would choose
either.

Donald.

```

"Donald Tees" <donald_tees@sympatico.ca>
> >
> > Not only cars, but under the most liberal of definitions, one could
claim
> > the bi-metallic strip in a toaster is a 'computer' as well as the light
> > switch on the wall.
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Fooey! I said 'under the most liberal of definitions...' Further, light
bulbs do require programming (ON - OFF) in the most elemental of programming
languages (ON-OFF). In fact, a light switch could easily be called a stored
program digital computer (under the most liberal of definitions(tm)). A
bi-metallic strip is a stored-program analog computer and it, too, had to be
'programmed' (bent properly).

If one wants to jack with definitions in the tradition of Humpty-Dumpty, a
book performs many of the functions of a computer: it stores and displays
data (sometimes it even contains bugs). A wooden block with two wires stuck
in it becomes WOM (write-only memory).
```

If you are going to include all items that can have a "state" as a computer,
why not include plants for their DNA?  DNA is a lot closer to a stored
program than a light bulb.

Few light bulbs have the capacity to read the state of their switches ... to
include a lightbulb as a computer requires that you include the human that
functions as the CPU.  Books ditto. Your definition of "liberal" could
include every atom in the universe, and certainly contains a painted, bare
wall that can be painted two colours.

You are just being obtuse, in my opinion.  Of course this is a newsgroup ...
being deliberately obtuse is par for the course.

Donald.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: What is COBOL done on?

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald_tees@sympatico.ca>
- **Date:** 2001-11-15T00:12:57-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Z1II7.20476$vR4.2856215@news20.bellglobal.com>`
- **References:** `<3BF27EFE.F526C206@Azonic.co.nz> <20011114230158.24267.00003294@mb-fv.aol.com>`

```
"YukonMama" <yukonmama@aol.com> wrote in message
news:20011114230158.24267.00003294@mb-fv.aol.com...
> >From: Richard Plinston riplin@Azonic.co.nz
> >Date: 11/14/01 9:26 AM Eastern Standard Time
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> Sorry to burst your bubble but modules on a favorite SUV produced by a 4
letter
> automaker run a highly modified version of Windows CE.

Now that brings on a chuckle.  It also brought back memories of a project I
did a long time ago that did close to the same thing. I do not remember the
date, but I would guess about 1982-3. Bill could probably verify that from
the Cobol compiler I used.

I was hired to build a one-up car computer for a prototype engine.  This was
not a prototype for a car computer, but lab test equipment going into a
vehicle.  I was handed a brand new mid sized american muscle car that had
been stripped down to bare metal, and told to put a computer in the back
seat.  I had 116 monitering points (discrete) and 64 analog sensors, each 12
bit.  I could do everything from reading torque sensors on each axle
(hydrolicly driven individual axles), to reading the air pressure at ten
points in the carburation, to using a gyroscope to sense vertical plane.
Real neat toy.

I bought two nineteen inch racks, and we cut them with a torch to fit, and
welded them in.  Then we mounted an S100 bus computer running MPM-86,
running with 640k. Under that was a 20 megabyte wincester drive.  That took
up the left rack.  The right rack took all our interfacing and metering.  By
the time I finished building the interfaces and the drivers, I could see the
data at the
S-100 bus level as a sequence of BCD digits, memory mapped.

We put an 72 character by 10 line gas plasma display in the dash on the
passeger side, and put a keyboard on a fold down tray-type hinge.  That was
the operators console. We put a second identical display on the dash for the
standard speed, odometer, etc, plus stuff like a ten second running average
of fuel usage.

All of the high speed stuff was done in 8086 assembler, and all of the
formating into various reports was done in Cobol.  It was Micro-Focus Cobol,
the same one that ran on the Altos Computer. I was able to set up the two
screens as ansi-terminals at the assembler level, and define them as such at
the Cobol level, then program them using screen sections.  Stuff like a
speedometer only has to be updated one or twice a second. The menus for the
monitoring stuff were written in Cobol, though the data monitoring was all
done in assembler.  The Cobol programs all saw their data magically appear
as memory disk. They would open a random file in input mode, and read record
zero.  I could sample all inputs at 400 hz, with everything being stored on
disk until it ran out.

That was twenty years ago, when computer power was expensive. My budget was
in the $300,000 range. The Cobol compiler was about $800.  Now they use
Windows in an actual vehicle, and I'll bet the computer costs less than
$100.  I see no reason why Cobol would not work on that computer, provided
each car buyer was willing to pay a $2500 royalty on the run-time system.

Times change, do they not?
Donald.
```

On 15-Nov-2001, "Donald Tees" <donald_tees@sympatico.ca> wrote:

> I believe that most libraries, even ones that charge, charge for borrowing
> physical books.

Huh?  I've never been to one that charged.

> I know of no libraries that pay fees to the owners of the
> dictionary of the language the books are written in.

If they did charge, I bet authors would demand royalties.

> And while most authors probably pay for a dictionary, they do not get
> charged for using the words

If the info I have is correct, if you attempt to modify your
code on an XP system, you will have to over-haul it. Not
being a VB programmer (well, ok, I've written a few lines of
VB code, but I won't call myself a VB programmer) I have to
take the word of someone who is (well, I assumed he was
considering...). What he said was, VB 6.0 and the new "VB#"
(XP version of VB) don't get along as VB 6 (and prior) are
not fully object oriented, while the XP VB is. Therefore,
things will not "compile". However, they might run when
loaded on an XP system, but they won't compile on an XP
system.

JerryP wrote:
<snip>
> "One platform:" - Which comprises 85% of the world's computers.
> "XP...re-written:" - How so? We run XP and VB. They were made for each
> other.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: What is COBOL done on?

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Grinder" <grinder@no.spam.maam.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T19:14:15-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9ssgou12en@enews4.newsguy.com>`
- **References:** `<3BF0B906.597F507F@Uni.com> <3BF11ECF.B59F86A@neo.rr.com> <7l9I7.40630$XR.2861623@bin3.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <3BF1B93E.7C2235B@neo.rr.com>`

```

"Steve Thompson" <sthompson_2@neo.rr.com> wrote in message
news:3BF1B93E.7C2235B@neo.rr.com...
> If the info I have is correct, if you attempt to modify your
> code on an XP system, you will have to over-haul it. Not
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> system.

It's true that VB6 code will not slide into VB.net, but the
applications and the compiler will still work.  An interface has
also been provided to make use of the .net architecture from
these "legacy" apps.

Porting a VB6 app to vb.net is roughly the same task we're
facing in taking a mpb Visual COBOL app to Fujitsu or
MicroFocus.

It boils down to this--if you keep your compiler working off the
same specifications, you have stability and can achieve a high
level of code re-use.  If you're free to develop new models, you
can leverage emerging technologies.  In this case, the brass
ring being sought is web services.

Perhaps this is not a profitable goal, but it would have been
foolish to attempt it in VB3's day--the marketplace and
infrastructure was simply not there.
```

<a id="t-0af097a789"></a>
## Thread: Aucocobol/Vision file system, reading a deleted record. — 6 msgs

### Aucocobol/Vision file system, reading a deleted record.

- **From:** fourwindsoh@geocities.com (Andrew Marks)
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T08:35:50-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<169f5f4b.0111130835.485a5ac7@posting.google.com>`

```
Is it possible to read deleted records, or undelete records, in a
Vision indexed file using available tools?  The current documentation
does not refer to such an action.

Sincerely,
Andy Marks
fourwindsoh@geocities.com
```

#### ↳ Re: Aucocobol/Vision file system, reading a deleted record.

- **From:** "Acucorp News" <shaun_gough@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T10:46:59-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1451C740A890D411B65C00104B95B1C0472DEA@ras.acucorp.com>`
- **References:** `<169f5f4b.0111130835.485a5ac7@posting.google.com>`

```
Dear Andrew.

Currently there is no way to read or undeleted a deleted record from a
Vision file, as the runtime removed the record pointer from the Vision
header segment, and the space used for the record is marked as available, so
that the space can be reused.

Also, if newer records have been added since some records are marked for
deletion, the deleted record space could already be used up by the newer
records, which will mean that there is no way to get the deleted records
back.

So, unfortunately, this is not possible.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Aucocobol/Vision file system, reading a deleted record.

- **From:** "Drake Coker" <drake@san.rr.com.nospam>

- **Message-ID:** `<nKCI7.35671$D5.13447569@typhoon.san.rr.com>`

```
Technically it is feasible, but not every time.  A lot depends on whether or
not
the original record was compressed or variable-size.  If so, then some
information
about the record is permanently lost when it is deleted, making
reconstruction
not entirely automatic.  It is this reason why Acucorp doesn't provide a
tool to do so.

However, that being said, it is technically possible to do much of the time.

Drake Coker

#### ↳ Re: Aucocobol/Vision file system, reading a deleted record.

- **From:** Vadim Maslov <vadik@siber.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-16T07:54:16+00:00

- **References:** `<169f5f4b.0111130835.485a5ac7@posting.google.com>`

```
AcuData2Flat converter from Siber Systems can read deleted
records and convert them to flat file (does not do it by default,
but there is a flag for it). That is, of course, if records
were not overwritten by newer records.

http://www.siber.com/sct/datafile/

Regards,
Vadim Maslov

## Thread: Mainframe to Excel — 13 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### Mainframe to Excel

- **From:** "Howard Brazee" <howard.brazee@cusys.edu>
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T20:24:26+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.ibm-main,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<_jfI7.2099$jp.323213@bin2.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
I have created comma delimited files for spreadsheets in the past, but not
for Excel.  I have created some files on the mainframe to be FTP'd to a PC
and read in by Excel.

I have some fields that contain commas, so I have been experimenting
unsuccessfully in formatting my file.

I have tried putting each field within single and double quotes, but I get
them in my output even though I tell Excel that they are text delimiters.  I
tell Excel to ignore successive delimiters and have my CoBOL program replace
real commas with pairs - but Excel doesn't seem to care.

I pulled out my green card to see if I could create a tab that would get
translated from EBCDIC to ASCII.

How do I format my file so that a user can FTP it from the mainframe and
import it into his spreadsheet the best way?
```

#### ↳ Re: Mainframe to Excel

- **From:** "Ron" <Ron@NoSpamForMe.Com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T14:59:57-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.ibm-main,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9ss1kk$pq8$1@suaar1ab.prod.compuserve.com>`
- **References:** `<_jfI7.2099$jp.323213@bin2.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
The import function of Excel allows you specify any delimiter.
Would it work to just use a semi-colon or a pipe "|" instead?
It also allows you import a fixed field format without delimiters.
You just have to specify the beginning and ending column positions
to Excel. That may not work though depending on your users as
they would have to (ahast!) know the record layout! As one of
my users put it: "What's a record layout?".
```

#### ↳ Re: Mainframe to Excel

- **From:** "Grinder" <grinder@no.spam.maam.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-13T19:07:30-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.ibm-main,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9ssgot02en@enews4.newsguy.com>`
- **References:** `<_jfI7.2099$jp.323213@bin2.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
vanilla CSV works well for me:

1)  Use " as the text delimiter, and the comma as a field
delimiter.
2)  Double all occurrences of the text delimiter.
3)  Enclose text in text delimiter.
4)  Format numerics such that they do not use the field
delimiter.
5)  Seperate fields with the field delimiter.

So, sample text would look like:

"Name", "DOB", "HourlyRate"
"Jake ""The Snake"" Plisken", 01/01/1960, 45.00

If you're not interested in providing formatting information
above what CSV can offer, you don't even have to use OLE to
drive Excel--you can just open the csv file, and it will
interpret the results.  Excel is not particularily typed, so
that can cause problems, but ones that can be worked around.

- **From:** jraben@cascinc.com (Jeff Raben)
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T19:22:00+00:00

"Howard Brazee" <howard.brazee@cusys.edu> wrote:

>I have created comma delimited files for spreadsheets in the past, but not
>for Excel.  I have created some files on the mainframe to be FTP'd to a PC
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
>import it into his spreadsheet the best way?

I've done it two ways when comma is a problem.
Xcel will parse on any delimiter.  
You can use x'09' (tab) or any other character not used on your line.
I use semi-colon ";" after translating all semi-colon on the "line" to
comma to get 'em out of the way.
When you go to import an ascii file, xcel's startup asks if the file
has fixed sized fields or is delimited...........

Jeff
and stir with a Runcible spoon...
```

#### ↳ Re: Mainframe to Excel

- **From:** "K Ledding" <kledding@eircom.net>
- **Date:** 2001-11-27T11:42:12
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.ibm-main,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<u%KM7.12559$8s4.56258@news.indigo.ie>`

"Howard Brazee" <howard.brazee@cusys.edu> wrote in message
news:_jfI7.2099$jp.323213@bin2.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com...

> them in my output even though I tell Excel that they are text delimiters.
I
> tell Excel to ignore successive delimiters and have my CoBOL program
replace
> real commas with pairs - but Excel doesn't seem to care.
>
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> import it into his spreadsheet the best way?

You might want to FTP it to a text file on the PC and then import it into MS
Access (get external data) and create a table.  When importing you can
specificy delimited or fixed width.  Then export from the table to the excel
spreadsheet.  I've done this before.

You can also set up an import specification within Access that can be
re-used so that you don't need to use the wizard each time you want to
import the data (it tells Access where each field begins and ends and what
format you want it in).

I have not done it using EBCIDIC data though, only text. If importing
numeric, it looks like the sign must appear first (i.e., -3000 not 3000-).

Good luck and let me know if this helps!
```

is
> at fault.

Thought I'd pass on more info about the Import Spec.

 When importing the data (file, get external data, import) select your text
file and work through the wizard.  Always pressing next instead of finish.
The wizard lets you define 'field options'.  This is where you tell it that
it is 'text' and not 'long integer'.  Thus it will keep your leading zeros.

At the end of the wizard, select 'advanced.'  It is here that you will see
the results of the wizard where you can 'save' your 'import spec.'  Then,
when importing again, the first screen of the wizard also has the 'advanced'
button.  Click that to get the import spec you saved.  At this point you
could 'finish'.  It will overwrite your old table (but it also adds primary
key... if you don't want one, continue to select 'next' to be sure to select
'no primary key').  Or, continue to the end and enter a new table name if
you don't want to overwrite the one you created previously.

Note that if Access does not like the way you defined a field for the data
it wants to import, it will create a separate error table.

When your table is ready to be 'exported' (file, export), select excel as
your file type.  The excel file will contain the Access field names in the
first row.  That should be it.  Good luck!
```

Sams Teach Yourself COBOL in 24 Hours
by Thane Hubbell

You can find it on Amazon.com.

I have used it, and have now passed it on to a fellow employee who is learning
COBOL.  Plus Thane is a frequent contributor here.  He has bailed me out a
couple of times too...... I'm sure if you had a question, and posted it, he
would be more then happy to help.

John

All of you in English speaking places other than the US and England, please
accept the fact that I *do* understand that what I am writing below has as
many variations as there are places that comprised the British Empire (de
facto and de jure).  However, let me limit this to these two "variations".

This week's news highlights this "issue".  Which movie is opening
  "Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone"
        or
  "Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone"
        ???

(Semi-)related to COBOL - does your "character based" screen system support
   Background-Color
       or
   Background-Colour
      or both?

How about Initialize or Initialise (or both) statements?  Organization or
Organisation for files?

***

When I worked on/with Micro Focus documentation, this UK-home-based company
had a company policy to use US spellings and format pages for 8 1/2 x 11 and
not A4 paper.  (Try getting a LARGE supply of "American Quarto" paper in the
UK !!!)

Bottom-Line:
  Whether Technical, fiction, or non-fiction - no matter where the author
lives/lived or wrote - the question of how much to "adapt" English in
"public documents" is something that I don't think will ever have an easy or
final answer.

P.S.  It is a "well known fact" that US English is "closer" to Elizabethan
(and/or Shakespearean) English than current UK (BBC, or King's or whatever)
English.  (cf. fall/autumn, deck/pack of cards, etc) If you go to
Appalachia, there is reasonable evidence that you even get Elizabethan
pronunciation as well as vocabulary.
```

"William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com> wrote in message

> (and/or Shakespearean) English than current UK (BBC, or King's or

> English.  (cf. fall/autumn, deck/pack of cards, etc) If you go to
> Appalachia, there is reasonable evidence that you even get Elizabethan
> pronunciation as well as vocabulary.

... And grammar.   I remember an anecdote from college relating that the
distinction between singular and plural second-person pronouns was retained
in the remoter areas of Appalachia (thou/thy-thine/thee vs.
you/your-yours/you) in some areas.  The anecdote was of a conversation
between a researcher and a "local" housewife, which didn't seem to involve
anything unusual, until the housewife looked up at the clock, said "Just a
moment", ran to the front door, opened it, and called out to her husband in
the field, "Marry, John!  Come get thy suppah!", complete with a trilled R
in the initial exclamation!

This is particularly interesting in that the *reconstruction* of a
distinction between the singular and the plural forms (you vs. y'all) occurs
not so very many leagues away ...

(I consider issues involving the formation of pronouns grammatical rather
than lexical ...)

    -Chuck Stevens
```

```
Many communities in Appalachia appear to have kept the dialect of the
original settlers, from whatever place and whatever time, in England.
The dialects can be very different in hollers ("Hollows" = valleys)
just a few miles apart.
The New York accent (Noo Yawk) was the accent of upper class London at
the time of the American Revolution.  Manhattan was occupied by the
British throughout most of the war, and the upper classes of the city
emulated the speech of the British Officers.
Most Quakers in Eastern USA can switch back and forth at will between
"you" and "thou", depending on to whom they are speaking.

Stephen J Spiro
```

They come from all over.  For example, Bette Davis (born Elizabeth

## Thread: Object References into CGI — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Web, XML, modern integration`](topics.md#web) · [`Tutorials, books, learning`](topics.md#learning)_

### Object References into CGI

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T15:36:57+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3bf1da75_5@news.newsgroups.com>`

```
I am currently developing a Web Application using Dynamic HTML.

The Scripting Object Model provides for Objects to be included on Web Pages
and these can include standard forms and controls and foreign Objects like
ActiveX controls.

I have had no difficulty in embedding ActiveX controls and referencing their
Attributes and Methods with VBScript and JavaScript.

For simple things like static drop down list boxes, Scripts are simple and
efficient.  For slightly more complex things Java Applets work fine.

However for validations and RDB access I intend to use CGI and thought that
COBOL might be good...

My first attempts succeeded and I had no difficulty in obtaining data
submitted from Web forms, in COBOL using a CGI interface. Neither do I have
any problem in writing HTML from the COBOL program and even have it creating
a dynamic page which includes a Java Applet to display some stuff...

My current problem is that I want to access Objects on the page DIRECTLY
from the CGI COBOL code. (This is a lot different to being passed the values
of certain of their attributes through the CGI interface.)

As an example (a real one...) I have a drop down list box on the web page
and its ID is "ListBox1". This object has a Method called "AddItem" which
enables lines to be added to the list. Using VBScript or JavaScript I can
invoke this Method without any problem at all, right on the HTML page. But I
can only add static lines to the box (Scripts are severely limited in what
they can do for file access...). I actually NEED to access an ISAM file (or
RDB table) and create a set of values (possibly as a Line Sequential file)
which can be added to the list box using the "AddItem" method. These values
will change according to who is accessing the Web page and from where...

Now, it isn't very hard to write a server side CGI COBOL program that does
all the file access and either creates a simple file to be loaded into the
list box or simply invokes the "AddItem" method directly as each record is
obtained.

BUT, in order to do this, I need an Object Reference to the List Box.

In VBScript I can say:        SET ObjRef = ListBox1
and the variable "ObjRef" will contain the Object Reference to the ListBox.

(I can also invoke the required method directly:  Listbox1.AddItem ("entry 1
in the box") ) This works beautifully and is fast and efficient with no
requirement for access back to the server.

I set up "ObjRef" as a Global Variable on the web page and ensured that the
above SET statement was activated before my COBOL program.

However, when I try and get the value of "ObjRef" through the CGI interface
I receive nothing, and my COBOL consequently fails when trying to invoke a
Method from a NULL Object Reference.

I COULD create an ActiveX object that automatically loads the List Box, and
simply not use the CGI at all, but this is more work than I would like at
the moment and I really would like to find out if it is possible to pass Web
Page Object References to the CGI.

Does anybody know of an EFFECTIVE way to get a Web Based Object reference
into a COBOL CGI script?

TIA

Pete.






-----=  Posted via Newsfeeds.Com, Uncensored Usenet News  =-----
http://www.newsfeeds.com - The #1 Newsgroup Service in the World!
 Check out our new Unlimited Server. No Download or Time Limits!
-----==  Over 80,000 Newsgroups - 19 Different Servers!  ==-----
```

## Thread: Closing the console window — 5 msgs

### Closing the console window

- **From:** floydj@netins.net (Floyd Johnson)
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T16:35:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9su6fp$c4m$1@ins22.netins.net>`

```
I am using Fujitsu COBOL v6.  The following subprogram, when called,
displays some simple demonstration data from a line sequential
file into the console window.  Is there some way to close the console
window after (or before) the "program exit" statement is executed and
control is returned to the calling program?  

The calling program uses a COBOL screen to control a menu (and in a later
version of the program, to gather some input data).  The length of the
input file is unknown.

Thank you for any advice.

Floyd Johnson


*>===============================================================

identification division.
program-id.                DisplayResults is initial.

environment division.
configuration section.
source-computer.           ibm-pc.
object-computer.           ibm-pc.

input-output section.
file-control.
    select datafile assign to "currdata.dat"
       organization is line sequential
       access mode is sequential
       file status is inp-file-status.
       
data division.
file section.
fd datafile.
01 input-record                     pic x(5).

working-storage section.
01 temp                             pic x(5).
01 EOF-flag                         pic x
               value "N".
01 inp-file-status                  pic xx value "00".
    88 file-success      value "00" thru "09".               

procedure division.
display-paragraph.
   *> Open the data file
   open input datafile
   
   *> Do an initial read
   perform read-record-paragraph
   
   *> Process the record until EOF
   perform until EOF-flag = "Y"

      *> Display the record
      move input-record to temp
      display temp
  
      *> Read the next record   
      perform read-record-paragraph
   end-perform
   
   *> Close the file 
   *>    and return to the calling program
   close datafile
   accept temp from console
   exit program
   .      

read-record-paragraph.
   read datafile
      at end move "Y" to EOF-flag
   .    

*>===============================================================
```

Try

@CBR_CONSOLE=SYSTEM (which should be the default)
@WinCloseMsg=ON

as environment variables.

## Thread: FILE-PREFIX — 1 msgs

### FILE-PREFIX

- **From:** chucks101@hotmail.com (Richard)
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T08:55:59-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bedd0b0e.0111140855.eae75c2@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi there,

I am editing the FILE-PREFIX variable under Windows 2000 and it
doesn't take the multiple paths I have entered.  The documentation
says you can enter up to 4096 chars. The last path gets truncated.

Here's an example;

FILE-PREFIX @server01:C:\myroot @server01:C:\myroot\dir1
@server01:C:\myroot\dir2 @server01:C:\myroot\dir3

Thanks.

## Thread: What is COBOL done on? — 1 msgs

### Re: What is COBOL done on?

- **From:** "James J. Gavan" <jjgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T18:02:25+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BF2B1E6.71C5031B@shaw.ca>`
- **References:** `<3BF0B906.597F507F@Uni.com> <3BF11ECF.B59F86A@neo.rr.com> <7l9I7.40630$XR.2861623@bin3.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <a50fcf68.0111131615.6dc62d6d@posting.google.com> <3BF27EFE.F526C206@Azonic.co.nz> <2IvI7.54335$Wa.3702688@bin1.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <RewI7.17075$vR4.2312860@news20.bellglobal.com> <9su5nd$15hdjs$1@ID-39799.news.dfncis.de> <3BF2A8B4.6F53189F@ils-international.com>`

```


COBOL Gold Mine at ILS International wrote:

> Localization? Internationalization? COBOL is Perhaps not 'the ONLY
> language with built-in multi-language support.', but certainly the
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> the world while listening to music in stereo!

I like the analogy to building a lift/elevator - it takes time. Those
who have been at COBOL a long time have learned to capture 'repetitive'
routines to be used as copyfiles or called sub-programs.

In this respect OO COBOL is no different BUT, for overall success it
does DEMAND lots of prior planning, which involves clearing the building
site, engineers/draughtsmen designing/drawing the building/elevator
specification - all this before the 'grunts' get down to the actual
construction. A lot of prior work - but the benefits show up in spades
later from this initial planning.

Pete Dashwood has illustrated the efficacy of Components. Same applies
with OO generally; arrive at a common design structure, say for editing,
printing, file/DB access, (the 'repetitives') and it makes the magic
word 'reusability' a truism.

Jimmy, Calgary AB
```

#### ↳ Re: MicroFocus Cobol 85 documents for making a project (school)

- **From:** chris.glazier@microfocus.com (Chris Glazier)
- **Date:** 2001-11-15T08:58:34-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<260cd566.0111150858.10c63b7a@posting.google.com>`

To which product are you referring? 

Micro Focus has many COBOL-85 compatible products on the market
including Net Express, Net Express UE, Workbench, Personal COBOL etc.

If you check out the microfocus.com web site you will find that you
can purchase a copy of Personal COBOL for your own use, at a very
reasonable price. It includes on-line documentation and help.

If you are looking for something a little more advanced then take a
look at Net Express University Edition.

## Thread: COBOL & PL/1........and JAVA — 10 msgs

### COBOL & PL/1........and JAVA

- **From:** "Rufio" <davecawdell@home.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-14T23:48:31+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<jpDI7.142776$B72.36543576@news1.rdc1.az.home.com>`

```
OK. So having started a different thread about working in COBOL & PL/1, I
started my new contract yesterday. Due to a Snafu with insurance (my agency
let it lapse), I'm having a day at home. I have a PL/1 book for company, and
I'm coming to a conclusion - keeping COBOL & PL/1 separate isn't hard - but
keeping PL/1 & JAVA separate does seem to be a problem. I have 15 years
COBOL, 0 years PL/1 & a few months self-study JAVA. But I keep coming upon
JAVA-like ideas such as data-type conversions that work differently in PL/1
& JAVA.

As we (Techies) are being required to do more & more multilingual coding,
how do we remember which rules apply to which languages. Or is my secret
supposition true - in a year or two, we will start to see specialized M/F,
Client-Server, OO & other programming posts?
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL & PL/1........and JAVA

- **From:** "James J. Gavan" <jjgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2001-11-15T02:11:10+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BF32475.FA22889D@shaw.ca>`
- **References:** `<jpDI7.142776$B72.36543576@news1.rdc1.az.home.com>`

```


Rufio wrote:

> OK. So having started a different thread about working in COBOL & PL/1, I
> started my new contract yesterday. Due to a Snafu with insurance (my agency
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> Client-Server, OO & other programming posts?

I nearly commented on your earlier message - suffice to say, "Jack of all
trades. Master of none...", in response to that one.

Can't address PL/1 because that's mainframe. But at least as regards Java, (I
believe) both Fujitsu and Net Express,  (and with their new V5, possibly also
Acu ), provide classes so that COBOL can talk to Java and vice versa - so that
kind of takes care of that problem. Additionally COBOL 2002 will be introducing
new data types, (Typedef for instance) that also address this problem.

Recall Pete Dashwood's recent message about CGI etc ? I know nothing about what
he's doing - but it shouldn't be so BLOODY complicated, should it. He's wanting
to take a very basic step, and has to turn himself into a rocket scientist to
find out the answer - and it really is bugger all to do with a problem in COBOL.

So much of this multilingual challenge is associated with MicroSloth. ("Ahh!",
says Billy, "Use my .Net fellas and all is solved". BS !).

Here's a neat little problem, don't know whether it is solely Micro Focus or
whether they are just paying lip service to how Windows APIs would handle it.
You folks using other Windows GUI tools - I'd be curious to know your answers.

I display a Material description (type of Metal, e.g. "ANSI AW3 4455 GR") and
have two droplists being the Type and Sub-Type, e.g. Type(0500)  = Copper and
Copper Alloy, Sub (0503)  =  Forgings and Fittings. Also have Type(0900) =
"Miscellaneous Type" and ONE entry only Sub(0901) = "Miscellaneous Sub-Type".

So for Sub I display the droplist (0901) - the one entry. And I see :-

        Miscellaneous Sub-Type
        Miscellaneous Sub-Type

Huh ? I've only got ONE ! Select the first - honky dory; select the second and I
go belly up - my index selection (2) from the SortedCollection used as the
droplist exceeds the collection size = 1. How the hell........

So check out the N/E help for droplists, " Sets the text in the entry field part
of the selection box to  lnkString. This also has the effect of adding the
string to  the list if it is not already included ".

Now isn't that really neat - so whichever object I display in the control box of
the droplist has to be IDENTICAL to an object already contained in the
Collection, or the new object gets added. (I was just pulling in the
description, but the elements in the Collection also contain the 4 digit code).

Is the problem just M/F or does this apply generally to droplists for GUIs ?

My concern is to produce a good BUSINESS system, and really don't want to be
diverted by irritating minutiae. If I really wanted to be a Windows artisan -
life would be a lot easier if I peddled off on my bike with a ladder, wet cloth
and a bucket !.

Jimmy
```

Some quick thoughts in response, Jimmy...

"James J. Gavan" <jjgavan@shaw.ca> wrote in message

> I nearly commented on your earlier message - suffice to say, "Jack of all

In the computer business it is becoming more necessary to be Master of
several trades and there is no room for Jack...<G> "Jack" goes broke pretty
fast when his incompetence is revealed...

> Can't address PL/1 because that's mainframe. But at least as regards Java,
(I
> believe) both Fujitsu and Net Express,  (and with their new V5, possibly
also
> Acu ), provide classes so that COBOL can talk to Java and vice versa - so
that
> kind of takes care of that problem. Additionally COBOL 2002 will be
introducing
> new data types, (Typedef for instance) that also address this problem.
>
(Personally, I see no need whatsoever for Typedef in COBOL and I don't see
COBOL data typing as a "problem"...but that's just me... for interfacing to
other software there MIGHT be a case, but I really see this as just another
excuse to "C"ify the language. Still, as it is in the 2002 standard, we
probably won't see it before 2020, anyway...<G>)

As far as Fujitsu goes, COBOL can "talk" to Java but in a limited way and
there is no capability for Java to invoke COBOL Classes. The Java Native
Interface (JNI) can be used to get from Java to COBOL but it is complex. An
interface utilising JNI is in my list of "things to do" but it is being
pushed down the priorities as I see a limited market for it and I have other
things to do at the moment.

 There is a limited market because most people will simply use Java where it
is appropriate to do so, so no interface to COBOL is really required. The
converse is not true because Java classes have facilities which COBOL
Classes currently don't and for which COBOL classes would need to be
written. It therefore makes sense to call Java from COBOL and I think that
is probably why Fujitsu have implemented a one-way interface (It also makes
the JNI behind the scenes much simpler...)

BOTTOM LINE: Don't hold your breath on full interactivity between Java and
COBOL... (Hit the Java books...<G>)

> Recall Pete Dashwood's recent message about CGI etc ? I know nothing about
what
> he's doing - but it shouldn't be so BLOODY complicated, should it.

I think you answered your own question here, Jimmy. It really ISN'T so
"bloody complicated"; it just seems like it if you know nothing about this
area. I have a workaround to the problem (which I figured out easily over a
coffee and a crossword) but I wanted there to be a better solution. It is
pretty basic OO programming; I just couldn't obtain the Object Reference and
it couldn't be instantiated as it already existed... It works now, but in
order to extend my own understanding I would like to see how or if it is
possible to address Objects in the Scripting Object Model directly from the
CGI.

> He's wanting
> to take a very basic step, and has to turn himself into a rocket scientist
to
> find out the answer - and it really is bugger all to do with a problem in
COBOL.
>

We all have to do that sometimes. Rockets are fun...<G>
(Actually, it is very much to do with a problem in CGI COBOL...)


> So much of this multilingual challenge is associated with MicroSloth.
("Ahh!",
> says Billy, "Use my .Net fellas and all is solved". BS !).
>

I'd be surprised if he's ever actually said THAT...<G> But I catch your
drift...
.NET will solve many of these problems and the "multilingual" thing will be
irrelevant. All we are interested in is functionality; all the system is
interested in is object code (or intermediate object code).

 The language used to develop it is irrelevant.  (HTML and XML components
are just around the corner and kids are learning  this at school...) The
next generation of COM  (ActiveX) and CORBA will lower the goalposts so
significantly that just about anyone will be able to place components on the
Web and have them work across platforms. SOAP (Simple Object Access
Protocol) is a step in this direction (I had a good look at it in response
to some advice from Thane, and liked it very much).

> Here's a neat little problem, don't know whether it is solely Micro Focus
or
> whether they are just paying lip service to how Windows APIs would handle
it.
> You folks using other Windows GUI tools - I'd be curious to know your
answers.
>
> I display a Material description (type of Metal, e.g. "ANSI AW3 4455 GR")
and
> have two droplists being the Type and Sub-Type, e.g. Type(0500)  = Copper
and
> Copper Alloy, Sub (0503)  =  Forgings and Fittings. Also have Type(0900) =
> "Miscellaneous Type" and ONE entry only Sub(0901) = "Miscellaneous
Sub-Type".
>
> So for Sub I display the droplist (0901) - the one entry. And I see :-
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> Huh ? I've only got ONE ! Select the first - honky dory; select the second
and I
> go belly up - my index selection (2) from the SortedCollection used as the
> droplist exceeds the collection size = 1. How the hell........
>
> So check out the N/E help for droplists, " Sets the text in the entry
field part
> of the selection box to  lnkString. This also has the effect of adding the
> string to  the list if it is not already included ".
>
> Now isn't that really neat - so whichever object I display in the control
box of
> the droplist has to be IDENTICAL to an object already contained in the
> Collection, or the new object gets added. (I was just pulling in the
> description, but the elements in the Collection also contain the 4 digit
code).
>
> Is the problem just M/F or does this apply generally to droplists for GUIs
?
>

Be careful here... are you talking about a combo box or a ListBox? Both of
them can have drop lists. If you simply want a drop down list that the user
can click on, that would be a ListBox; if the user can enter a string and
see the list scroll to the point matching the entry string, that would be a
combo box (Windows terminology, not Vendor or language specific).

I think you are talking a combo box but cannot be sure from the description.

It appears that if the user enters a string which is not in the Collection
the droplist has been loaded from, the new entry is added to the droplist
AND the Collection???

That would be specific to MF. There should be some attributes or Methods you
can use to stop this. Can you look at the combo control's attributes with an
Object Browser?

For example, one of the combo box controls I use has an attribute called
"IsQuery". If this is TRUE, only data which matches the string being entered
by the user will be displayed in the droplist. Setting it FALSE allows the
User to input data which does not currently exist. However, this data would
not be automatically added to the source Collection/File, neither would it
be added to the droplist... What happened to it would depend on what Methods
or code I invoked on the "Return" or "SelChange" events...

> My concern is to produce a good BUSINESS system, and really don't want to
be
> diverted by irritating minutiae.

It's a worthwhile goal, Jimmy. However, if you find the details of
programming to be "irritating minutiae" maybe you should keep yourself as a
Business Analyst and hand the rest over to a Programmer?

If you can't stand the heat...<G>


> If I really wanted to be a Windows artisan -
> life would be a lot easier if I peddled off on my bike with a ladder, wet
cloth
> and a bucket !.
>

...'specially in the summer...<G>

Pete.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL & PL/1........and JAVA

- **From:** Paul Barnett <paul.barnett@microfocus.nospam.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-16T17:50:30+00:00

- **Message-ID:** `<3BF551E6.6D16D3BB@microfocus.nospam.com>`
- **References:** `<jpDI7.142776$B72.36543576@news1.rdc1.az.home.com> <3BF32475.FA22889D@shaw.ca> <3bf34e2b_2@goliath.newsgroups.com>`

```
Peter,

You said "As far as Fujitsu goes, COBOL can "talk" to Java but in a limited way
and
there is no capability for Java to invoke COBOL Classes. "

This may be true but I must point out that Net Express 3.1 from Micro Focus
*does* include this capability as does Server Express 2.0.10 and later.

Micro Focus provide a Java import that includes various classes and methods,
particularly cobCall class. The class wizard in NetExpress helps you to wrap
existing cobol code in Java for use in distributed applications. An example of
where it's useful to do this is where a Java Swing based GUI interface that
works across an intranet or the internet. The user interface works uses the
standard Java techniques for calling processes on the server which could be
cobol from a legacy system. Many micro Focus customers have chosen this route
for modernise and web enable existing systems.

Some people prefer this approach to using HTML and CGI because of the extra
control and interaction you can have between the aplication code and the user
interface that you can get with Java.

Also, I agree that using CGI with COBOL is not complicated. Net Express make
this surprisingly easy.

Regards,
Paul

Why would you expect PL/1 and Java to "work the same", Rufio?

Give yourself some time. You are being exposed to some "non-COBOL" concepts.
At first, they are difficult, but later it becomes understood.

The funny thing is that your COBOL ability will benefit from some of these
concepts too.

You are probably correct that there will be specialized jobs advertised in
the not-too-distant future. There are such jobs today..."Mainframe Systems
Programmer", "Web Integration Specialist", "Network Administrator"...
It doesn't cause most of us any concern.

The more knowledge you acquire, the more valuable you become.

It really depends on your attitude to learning. I find learning new things
fun...therefore have little difficulty with it. Others see learning as
necessary to do a job and will sweat it all the way.

I remember complaining to my Boss many years ago about being exhausted by a
new intensive course I was sent on. (It was in NCR 500 machine language and
I had to do what was intended to be a 3 week course in 5 days from audio
tapes...I was dreaming it <G>). I still smile at what he said to me:

"If what we do was "easy", anybody could do it and they wouldn't need us..."

Hang in there!

Pete.

```

On 14-Nov-2001, "Rufio" <davecawdell@home.com> wrote:

> As we (Techies) are being required to do more & more multilingual coding,
> how do we remember which rules apply to which languages. Or is my secret
> supposition true - in a year or two, we will start to see specialized M/F,
> Client-Server, OO & other programming posts?

Even with my "native" programming languages (ones that I can put aside for a
decade and come back to without referring to a book), I have this confusion.
  So I keep a cheat sheet:

I work at an IDMS shop.  We have 3 different sets of 88 levels of IDMS error
status, the standard Cobol one, the standard ADS/O one, and one which was
supplied by Pinnacle with programs they wrote (dumb).   So I printed out
these status codes and keep them handy when I try to remember whether to use
DB-ANY-ERROR, ANY-ERROR-STATUS, or DML-NON-ABORT-ERROR.

Your cheat sheet will be different.  You will know what features of the
languages are similar enough to mess you up.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL & PL/1........and JAVA

- **From:** gah@ugcs.caltech.edu (glen herrmannsfeldt)
- **Date:** 2001-11-16T01:54:15+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9t1rk7$7l0@gap.cco.caltech.edu>`
- **References:** `<jpDI7.142776$B72.36543576@news1.rdc1.az.home.com>`

```
"Rufio" <davecawdell@home.com> writes:

>OK. So having started a different thread about working in COBOL & PL/1, I
>started my new contract yesterday. Due to a Snafu with insurance (my agency
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>& JAVA.

>As we (Techies) are being required to do more & more multilingual coding,
>how do we remember which rules apply to which languages. Or is my secret
>supposition true - in a year or two, we will start to see specialized M/F,
>Client-Server, OO & other programming posts?

Java seems to have been designed to stay close to C in many ways,
especially in expression evaluation rules.  

PL/I has completely different expression evaluation rules than the
other languages.  They are different enough that you won't have so
much trouble remembering when to use them.  

If you can explain the value of the constant expression 25+1/3 you
are most of the way there.  (I hope this hasn't changed over the years.)

Note also that there is a cobol compiler to generate JVM code, so
maybe you can interface Java and COBOL.  No JVM generating PL/I
compiler yet.

-- glen
```

Since it is PL/1 which follows the Fortran mathematic rules, I believe
it is 25 + (1/3).  The division has priority over the addition so the
1 divided by 3 would be done first with the quotient added to 25.
In fact, I believe it would be done the same in Cobol.  Like you, I
have always used parenthesis to separate my mathematics functions so
there is no guessing.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL & PL/1........and JAVA

- **From:** Volker Bandke <vbandke@bsp-gmbh.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-17T16:11:25+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<m4vcvtsvirqkkss4pfhft2al4bisq44l7p@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<jpDI7.142776$B72.36543576@news1.rdc1.az.home.com> <9t1rk7$7l0@gap.cco.caltech.edu> <TJ8J7.148$%o.99430@paloalto-snr1.gtei.net>`

```
On Fri, 16 Nov 2001 13:43:15 GMT, "Michael Mattias"
<michael.mattias@gte.net> wrote:

>glen herrmannsfeldt <gah@ugcs.caltech.edu> wrote in message
>news:9t1rk7$7l0@gap.cco.caltech.edu...
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>


Of course, PLI uses the mathematical rules, i.e. 25+1/3 = 25 + (1/3).

The interesting thing, though, (and that is what Glen probably had in
mind) is that you won't get what you expect:

PUT SKIP LIST(25+1/3) will not display 25.333333333 or something
similar, but will do one of the following

- ABEND (S0CA)
- displays 5.33333333333333

If the default FIXEDOVERFLOW condition processing is active at the
time the instruction is executed, you get the abend, else you get the
(truncated) result.

BTW, it gets even more interesting if you then try

PUT SKIP LIST(25+001/3);

"Carol La Biche" <ulyqr@salon.com> wrote in message

But having the capability to do it doesn't mean that I DO do it.  Having a
gun in your house doesn't mean you shoot people. (It means you COULD...<G>)

> And you resent the fact that hundreds of thousands of nobodies now find
> it correspondingly easier to contact you?

Nope. I'm generally very happy for people to contact me. However, this
access is contingent on their reason for doing so. Just because I will
accept "Hello!" from a total stranger, doesn't mean I will then stop and let
him sell me something...


> This is worse than snobbery; this
> is "access greed": wanting to have access to others for yourself but for
them
> not to have access to you.
>
It is neither snobbery nor greed. I don't spam people. Why should people
spam me?

It is interesting that the author of this note accuses anti-spammers of
greed; the motivation for the spam in the first place is cheap access to a
vast potential market without respect or regard for the privacy or time of
the people in it. This constitutes greed without even consideration.

> This is the dirty secret of the anti-spammers.
>
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>

This is such a pathetic attempt it is hardly worth refuting.

Freedom of Speech is a noble idea for which countless thousands of men and
women have given their lives in the course of history.

No reasonable person would want to curtail another's right to freedom of
expression and opinion. Even when we disagree, we still accept that hearing
unpalatable messages is part of the cost of Democracy. If we accept the
system, we accept the downside. ("I may not agree with what you say, but I
shall defend to the Death your right to say it...").

Does sending unsolicited advertising to a couple of million "prospects" come
in this category?

I don't think so.

Why not?

Because the "message" is frivolous, and telling me about it is not a serious
expression of opinion on the part of the spammer, who is doing it for money,
and in the hope of obtaining even more money...

I am therefore not required to pay serious attention to spam and my failure
to do so can in no way be called an infringement of the spammer's Democratic
right to Freedom of Speech.

My policy on spam is to respond politely and request removal from the list.

I will do that twice.

After that it becomes ugly... So far, I have disabled one spam server for 36
hours and threatened two others.  I am no longer troubled by these three.

Fair warning was given (in two different languages <G>). I consider this
defending my right to Peace and the Pursuit of Happiness, nothing to do with
Free Speech <G>

Newsgroups are much more difficult because they are by design intended to be
open and we, as subscribers, have no control over them.

It is good to see recent anti-spam posts here, and interesting that this
plea on behalf of Spam was made after such a post. Obviously, it was
effective...

Pete.

> Free speech -- as long as it has a nice, secure one-way valve attached?
>

lane.

you'll get a whole panoply of responses varying from marketer to marketer. I
concede many are in fact motivated by a desire for money. I just think
assuming the motivation of all based on the motivation of the few is unwise.

<a id="t-27eca227cf"></a>
## Thread: TAB expansion in current Micro Focus (MERANT) products — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### TAB expansion in current Micro Focus (MERANT) products

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-11-15T09:16:21-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9t0mej$6lp$1@slb4.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
As a follow-up on another thread, I have been having a discussion with
various parts of Micro Focus concerning TAB expansion in the current
products.  (This is NOT necessarily true of earlier products - such as
Microsoft COBOL).  The following is the summary that "we" have come up with
(and which will be reflected in some future MF documentation)

   ***

A) The LRM is in ERROR.  The T run-time switch *never* impacts the handling
of TABs on a READ (of LINE SEQUENTIAL files).  (It does impact the WRITE -
and REWRITE statements)

B) The EXPANDTAB/INSERTAB feature is only available for the "NetExpress,
Mainframe Express, and Server Express external file handlers"

C) When EXPANDTAB is set to "off" in the NE, MFE and SX external file
handler
configuration file, then tabs are NOT expanded (for line sequential files)
on READs - in all other cases, they are.

D) For Object COBOL, there is (currently) *no* way to avoid TAB expansion on
READs.

  ***

Sorry for any confusion that my "vague memories" or reading of conflicting
documentation may have caused.
```

#### ↳ Re: TAB expansion in current Micro Focus (MERANT) products

- **From:** Paul Barnett <paul.barnett@microfocus.nospam.com>

- **References:** `<9t0mej$6lp$1@slb4.atl.mindspring.net>`

```

Paul

## Thread: IBM VACOBOL and calling DLLs — 3 msgs

### IBM VACOBOL and calling DLLs

- **From:** bneumann@usu.de (Bernd W. Neumann)
- **Date:** 2001-11-16T01:31:39-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<664ab028.0111160131.7b245f8d@posting.google.com>`

```
I need to call DLL functions from within COBOL, however the only
sample to be found is that of a single entry DLL, where DLL name and
entry name match. Is there a way to specify entry name apart from DLL
name, for DLLs with multiple entries (which I think is the standard)?

Help or links would be greatly appreciated.

Bernd W. Neumann
```

#### ↳ Re: IBM VACOBOL and calling DLLs

- **From:** JAndersen@screenio.com (John Andersen)
- **Date:** 2001-11-16T23:53:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3bf5a46b.88356302@192.168.2.2>`
- **References:** `<664ab028.0111160131.7b245f8d@posting.google.com>`

```
On 16 Nov 2001 01:31:39 -0800, bneumann@usu.de (Bernd W. Neumann) wrote:

 >I need to call DLL functions from within COBOL, however the only
 >sample to be found is that of a single entry DLL, where DLL name and
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
 >Bernd W. Neumann

This is more of a linking issue than a cobol issue.
You usually have a small "exports library" associated
with a dll that is used when linking.  This library
knows what entry points are in the dll and sets
up the proper calling.

In the absence of this, the convention varies
by compiler, but us usually something along
the lines of knowing or finding the entry address
(via GetProcAddress if in windows) and then doing the
call "indirectly" to that address. Some compilers
supply utilities for this, others don't.


John Andersen
NORCOM
http://www.SCREENIO.com/
Juneau, Alaska
```

#### ↳ Re: IBM VACOBOL and calling DLLs

- **From:** Colin Campbell <cmcampb@attglobal.net>
- **Date:** 2001-11-16T21:13:17-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BF5F1ED.723201A8@attglobal.net>`
- **References:** `<664ab028.0111160131.7b245f8d@posting.google.com>`

```
Bernd,
It's been about 18 months, and I was using V2.2, but as I recall, one
subroutine per DLL is all that VA COBOL allows.  That's a pretty small
library!  You need to have a directory that contains all of the DLL's
that your driver program will be calling.

Also, driver programs MUST be EXE's, and subroutines MUST be DLL's.
Colin

…[5 more quoted lines elided]…

#### ↳ Re: Free DOS COBOL Compiler

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2001-11-22T04:06:04+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BFC7973.1D26F5D@worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<3bf562fa$0$32588$626a54ce@news.free.fr>`

```
Bernard Giroud wrote:
> 
> A friend of us (Tinycobol project developers) (I think it was Jim Powell)
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> Bernard Giroud

I downloaded it, but I haven't tried it out yet.  Documentation is
available in English or French.  It supports an odd format, AREA A
begins in Column 1.  It apparently supports the SORT verb, but does
not support the SEARCH verb or indexed files.  The compiler generates
x86 assembler code, which is then assembled and linked with the
supplied assembler and linker.  I think all the files I downloaded
(most are zipped) will fit comfortably on a single 1.44 meg floppy
disk.

I think a nice feature is that you can download the source code for
the compiler itself, which appears to be written in Borland C.  So it
might be possible to modify the compiler to suit your needs.
```

<a id="t-81c85d4e2f"></a>
## Thread: Finding LOCAL-STORAGE and/or BLK cells — 10 msgs

### Finding LOCAL-STORAGE and/or BLK cells

- **From:** "David de Jongh" <ddejongh@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2001-11-17T14:26:02+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<_ruJ7.173437$3d2.7303551@bgtnsc06-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
We are converting most of our COBOL for OS/390 programs to use LOCAL-STORAGE
instead of WORKING-STORAGE.  In a static link of about 800 programs, we've
cut down our overall storage use by 6MB (about 80%) and cut CPU time by
about 20%.  This is because local storage is made available to other
programs on return from a call, rather than being retained as part of the
program's "last-used state", with the resultant serial search each time a
program is called.
My problem is in my condition handler routine, which formats an "intelligent
mini-dump", including control blocks and other areas that are specific to
our environment, as well as key COBOL areas.  I can find working storage
easily enough (start of working storage is a TGT+X'114', then add 4k until
you've exhausted the length at TGT+X'68'), but the BLK cells and local
storage itself are in the variable part of the DSA and the location (like
many other things) is not documented in any of the LE or COBOL for OS/390
manuals.  They are mapped in the program listing, of course, but that's no
help at run-time.
There is obviously a way to find the BLK cells, because they are displayed
in an AbendAid dump.  Does anyone know how to find them?
D de J
```

#### ↳ Re: Finding LOCAL-STORAGE and/or BLK cells

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 2001-11-19T05:55:30+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20011119005530.07128.00000647@mb-bh.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<_ruJ7.173437$3d2.7303551@bgtnsc06-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
David de Jongh writes ...

>We are converting most of our COBOL for OS/390 programs to use LOCAL-STORAGE
>instead of WORKING-STORAGE.  In a static link of about 800 programs, 

Wow!. Out of curiosity, why are you static linking this many progams?


>we've
>cut down our overall storage use by 6MB (about 80%) and cut CPU time by
>about 20%.  This is because local storage is made available to other
>programs on return from a call, 

I don't understand this sentence. On return from a call, the called program's
local storage is unavailable, I should think. Local-storage is allocated on
entry to a routine, and freed on exit. At least, that's my understanding. If
so, how could local storage be "made available to other programs"?


>rather than being retained as part of the
>program's "last-used state", with the resultant serial search each time a
>program is called.

What "serial search" are you talking about?


>My problem is in my condition handler routine, which formats an "intelligent
>mini-dump", including control blocks and other areas that are specific to
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>in an AbendAid dump.  Does anyone know how to find them?

If they are not documented and the AbendAid folks can do it, it must be
documented in a pub that you pay extra money for. Good luck getting it for
free.

Of course, you could declare a pointer in working-storage and SET that pointer
to a local-storage item on entry; then you could get to it - if every program
followed this convention.

Regards,


Steve Comstock
